===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/access-monetization-layer.md =====

# **Access & Monetization Layer**
## **Overview**

This layer defines how users gain access to certain features and how financial support translates into NUMBERS and access conditions within the system.

It connects:

* real-world contribution

* in-system currency (NUMBERS)

* feature access and depth of participation

---

## **NUMBERS Acquisition**

Users obtain NUMBERS through two main sources:

* direct financial contribution (e.g. donations, subscriptions)

* participation rewards (granted through activity or specific mechanics)

Financial contribution provides the baseline value reference for NUMBERS.

---

## **Value Reference**

The system follows a simple baseline:

* 1 NUMBERS ≈ €0.01

Example:

* €2.10 → 210 NUMBERS

This baseline ensures:

* predictable value

* consistent pricing across features

* clear user understanding of cost

---

## **Feature Access Model**

Some protected features require spending NUMBERS to access.

**Example**:

* Explorer access requires a time-based fee

This creates a paid, time-limited access model for higher-value tools.

It keeps access intentional rather than passive.

---

### **Current Pricing Example: Explorer**

The Explorer is the main current example of this access model.

Current Explorer pricing:

* Standard access cost: **21 NUMBERS**

* Access duration: **21 minutes**

**This creates:**

* a paid, time-limited access model for a higher-value tool

* more focused exploration

* intentional use instead of passive browsing

---

## **Participation-Based Pricing**
Users with sufficiently high cumulative participation can unlock reduced pricing for certain protected features.

Current example:

Explorer access

* Standard cost: **21 NUMBERS**

* Reduced cost: **3 NUMBERS**

Discount eligibility is based on the user’s total NUMBERS spent in the system.

**Example threshold:**

* **4410 NUMBERS** (= €21 donated) **total spent → reduced Explorer pricing unlocked**

---

The access layer is not limited to flat pricing. Some mechanics also use percentage-based pricing, such as digout at 21% of the total NUMBERS previously spent on a challenge.

---

## **Purpose of the Pricing Model**

This pricing model is designed to make feature access meaningful, structured, and proportional to user involvement.

It serves to:

* assign a NUMBERS cost to high-value web tools

* reward sustained participation through reduced pricing

* keep access intentional rather than frictionless

* support a progression model where sustained involvement unlocks better access conditions over time

The Explorer is the main current example of this logic, and the same model can extend to other paid features as the system grows.

---

## **Role in the Product**

The Access & Monetization Layer connects:

* financial contribution

* NUMBERS accumulation

* feature access

* progression benefits

It gives the system a way to structure how users move from simple participation to deeper access and lower-friction use of protected features.

---

## **Product Impact**

This layer ensures that:

* system usage remains intentional

* financial support, participation, and feature access remain aligned

* access to powerful tools reflects user involvement

It reinforces the idea that:

interaction is not frictionless by default; it is structured by user involvement over time.


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/auction-and-digout-system.md =====

# **Auction & Digout System**
## **Purpose**

This system allows the community to bypass normal challenge progression in specific cases by reviving archived ideas or forcing execution priority through collective support.

---

## **Auction**
An auction is a threshold-based execution mechanic.

### **How it works**
the streamer can assign a challenge a NUMBERS threshold

the community can collectively contribute toward that threshold

if the threshold is reached, the challenge is immediately selected for execution

### **Role in the system**

Auction creates a strategic override on top of the normal ranking system.

**It:**

* encourages collaboration around a shared execution goal  
* creates a high-cost spending path for challenges the community wants strongly enough  
* gives the streamer a flexible override tool for challenges that may seem difficult, marginal, or not worth executing under normal conditions  
* makes community demand more legible by showing which challenges can attract unusually strong collective support

### **Selection logic**

A high threshold can also act as a demand test: if a challenge seems especially hard or not immediately relevant, the community must show stronger support to justify execution.

---

## **Digout**
Digout is the revival mechanic for archived challenges.

### **How it works**

an archived challenge can be revived by paying a percentage of its historical NUMBERS support

once revived, the challenge keeps its previously accumulated total NUMBERS support instead of returning to zero

### **Role in the system**

Digout prevents strong ideas from disappearing permanently after one failed cycle.

**It:**

* restores past support  
* gives previously backed challenges a return path that preserves the value already spent on them  
* prevents the system from treating each challenge cycle as if the past support never happened

---

## **Archive and Revival Logic**
### **Archive conditions**
A challenge moves to Archived when:

* it reaches the end of its 21-day active window without enough promotion

* an auctioned challenge fails to reach its required NUMBERS threshold

### **Digout cost**
Any user can revive an Archived challenge by paying 21% of the total NUMBERS previously spent on that challenge.

### **Support restoration**

A successful digout does not restart the challenge from zero.

The challenge keeps its previously accumulated total NUMBERS support.

### **Why this matters**

Because challenge ranking is based on total NUMBERS spent, restoring historical support allows a revived challenge to return immediately to the competitive pool instead of rebuilding support from scratch.

---

## **Purpose in the product**

Together, Auction and Digout add strategic recovery and override mechanics to the product.

They ensure the challenge system is not only linear, but resilient and dynamic over time.


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/challenge-removal.md =====

# **Challenge Removals**
## **Purpose**

Challenge removal allows the original author of a challenge to withdraw it from the active system under defined conditions.

This is not only a cleanup action. It is also an economic and strategic feature that:

* lets authors stop backing ideas they no longer want to keep active  
* creates refund distribution choices  
* allows part of the removed value to be redirected toward the author, the pushers, or the Community Chest

## **Who can use it**

Only the original challenge author can remove a challenge.

This means:

* removals are author-controlled  
* other users cannot remove someone else’s challenge  
* the action is tied to challenge ownership, not general moderation power

## **When removal is allowed**

A challenge can only be removed when it is still in a removable state.

In practice, removal is blocked for challenges that are already:

* Archived  
* Auctioned  
* Completed  
* Failed  
* In Progress  
* Removed

This means removal remains an author-side decision during the active life of a challenge, not something that happens after the challenge has already reached a final state.

## **What removal does**

When a valid removal happens:

* the challenge moves to the Removed state  
* the challenge becomes non-interactable  
* the challenge is terminated as an active progression object  
* a 21% refund amount is calculated from the NUMBERS previously spent on the challenge

The refund is not a full reversal.  
 It is a partial redistribution mechanic based on prior spending.

## **Refund calculation**

When a challenge is removed, the system calculates one refund amount equal to 21% of the NUMBERS previously spent on pushes for that challenge.

That refund amount is then divided into:

* **the author’s share**, based on the author’s own push contribution  
* **the pushers’ share**, based on the contribution made by other pushers

That refund amount is then distributed according to the selected refund option.

## **Refund distribution options**

The author chooses how the calculated refund is distributed.

#### **community\_forfeit**

100% goes to the Community Chest

#### **author\_and\_chest**

the author receives their share; the rest goes to the Community Chest

#### **author\_and\_pushers**

the author receives their share; the rest goes back to pushers

## **Command input**

When removal is triggered through chat command flow, the author selects the refund option as part of the remove command.

This keeps the removal decision:

* explicit at the moment of removal  
* tied to one chosen refund path  
* consistent with the command-driven interaction model

## **Role in the system**

Challenge removal adds a controlled exit path for submitted ideas.

It allows the system to:

* let authors withdraw an active challenge they no longer want to keep in play  
* return part of the previously committed value instead of treating that value as fully lost  
* create strategic choices around whether that returned value benefits the author, the pushers, or the Community Chest  
* encourage stronger follow-through during the active life of a challenge, because both the author and the pushers can have value tied to how the idea performs

This makes challenge authorship more meaningful, because the author keeps agency over an idea after submission, while pushers are also incentivized to track what happens to the challenge over time.

It also makes author commitment more visible, because other users can take the author’s own involvement and removal behavior into account before deciding to support a challenge.

## **Economic role**

Challenge removal is also an economic feature.

It can:

* return part of the value to the author  
* return part of the value to pushers  
* redirect part or all of that value to the Community Chest

This makes removal more than a simple delete action.

It turns withdrawal into a structured redistribution mechanic inside the NUMBERS economy.

## **Product impact**

This feature ensures that:

* challenge authors keep agency over their own proposals  
* abandoned or unwanted ideas can leave the system in a structured way  
* prior support can still create value after removal  
* removal becomes part of the product’s strategic and social economy, not just a destructive action 


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/challenge-submission.md =====

# **Challenge Submission**
## **Purpose**

Challenge Submission is the entry point for new challenges in the system.  

It allows users to introduce ideas that can later be reviewed, promoted, explored, and potentially executed.

---

## **What users can do**

Users can:

* submit structured challenges

* define whether a challenge is one-off or recurring

* specify cadence and duration for recurring challenges

* introduce new directions for the streamer and the community

---

## **Submission structure**
Each challenge follows a structured format:

* Goal → the high-level objective

* Instructions → the execution details

* Constraints → optional rules or limitations

* References → optional supporting material

This structure makes challenges clearer, easier to compare, and easier for the system to process consistently.

---

## **Challenge Scope and Examples**

Challenges can cover many types of objectives, including:

* rudiments  
* songs  
* styles  
* fills  
* techniques  
* musician studies  
* other creative tasks

They can also include modifiers such as:

* blindfolded  
* one hand  
* inverted  
* stick tricks

### **Purpose in the system**

This keeps the system broad enough for variety while preserving a comparable structure.

---

## **Validation logic**
Submissions are not fully free-form. The system currently enforces:

* minimum challenge text length

* structured input fields

* required titles for references

* validation before the challenge enters the system

This limits malformed or low-effort submissions, with stricter validation planned later.

---

## **Review entry conditions**
Some challenges do not enter the normal Active state immediately.

Depending on the rules in place, they may first enter an Under Review state.

This can happen for example when:

* structure or references require additional validation  
* a submission triggers a higher review-sensitivity rule  
* future rules require review for specific submission categories

**Under Review** does not always mean the challenge is fully frozen.

Depending on the rule, it may still remain visible and partially interactable.

---

## **Cost system**

Submitting a challenge requires spending NUMBERS.

The cost follows a dynamic model:

* repeated submissions increase in cost

* the cost resets daily

This encourages more intentional participation and discourages spam or low-effort submissions.

===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/demo-access-mode.md =====

## **Demo Access Mode**
Challenge Submission also supports a restricted Demo Access Mode.

In this mode:

* selected demo users enter through dedicated demo perennial tokens

* demo/test tokens are recognized by the backend

* the normal protected submission flow is preserved

* the submit form can enable a guided demo submission flow

* this flow allows the form to be progressively prefilled step by step, reducing typing during demos while preserving the feel of real interaction

This creates a fast and controlled showcase flow without bypassing the real submission system.

---

## **Role in the system**

Challenge Submission feeds the entire system.

It creates new opportunities for interaction, keeps ideas flowing into the product, and provides the raw material for promotion, competition, and execution.

---

## **Product impact**

This ensures that:

* users actively shape the system

* content originates from the community

* participation starts with creation, not just reaction

# **Demo Access Mode**

# **Demo Access Mode**

The system also supports a restricted **Demo Access Mode** for onboarding, internal testing, and product showcases.

## **What it allows**

* selected demo users can enter the standard product flow using dedicated demo perennial tokens

* demo users can submit challenges through the same protected submission flow as regular users

* demo users can access the Explorer through the same gated access flow

* demo/test perennial tokens are recognized by the backend and can enable a **guided demo submission flow** in the challenge submit form

* in this mode, the form can be progressively prefilled step by step through right-arrow input, allowing a fast and fluid demonstration without manual typing

## **Current restriction model**

* demo Explorer sessions only expose the restricted demo dataset

* this dataset currently contains:

  * challenges submitted by demo-scoped users

  * seeded / preloaded demo challenges used to make the environment immediately explorable

## **Purpose in the system**

This creates a safe way to let people experience real product behavior without exposing the full live dataset.

## **Product impact**

* makes the system easier to test  
* makes the product easier to demonstrate  
* provides a smoother onboarding and showcase flow  
* offers an accessible entry point before exposing the full live environment


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/explorer.md =====

# **Explorer – Challenge Discovery Interface**
## **Purpose**

The Explorer is the main interface where users browse, evaluate, and compare challenges across the entire system.

It acts as a strategic layer, helping users decide where to apply their influence.

---

## **What it is**

The Explorer is a structured view of all challenges in the system.

It allows users to:

* access the full history of submitted challenges

* compare challenges based on support, status, and activity

* identify opportunities to influence outcomes

---

## **Core Functions**

Users can:

* browse challenges ranked by configurable metrics (default: most recently updated)

* filter and explore challenges across multiple dimensions (status, activity, and system metrics)

* inspect detailed challenge data (content, status, activity, duration, and cadence)

* identify where influence can be applied

---

## **Role in the system**

The Explorer turns challenge data into a decision-making tool.

It creates:

* competition between challenges

* challenges gain or lose visibility based on community support and activity

* a direct link between user actions and system outcomes

It is where users shift from passive browsing to strategic participation.

---

## **Explorer Entry Fee**

Access to the Explorer requires a NUMBERS fee.

* Standard access cost: **21 NUMBERS per 21 minutes**

* Reduced cost: **3 NUMBERS per 21 minutes** for eligible users

This pricing:

* reinforces the value of Explorer access

* encourages intentional usage rather than passive browsing

* gives sustained participation a visible benefit

---

## **Demo Access Mode**

The Explorer also supports a restricted demo mode.

### **How it works**

**Demo users:**

* enter through dedicated demo perennial tokens

* follow the normal Explorer verification and paid-access flow

* can still submit challenges through the normal submission flow

* only see the restricted demo dataset inside Explorer

### **Current dataset scope**

The demo Explorer dataset currently includes:

* challenges submitted by demo-scoped users

* seeded demo challenges used to keep the Explorer immediately usable

### **Why it exists**

This allows users to experience the real Explorer and challenge-submission flow without exposing the full live challenge database.

---

## **Explorer access flow**

### **Explorer access now uses a two-layer model:**

* token-gated identity verification  
* separate paid access entitlement window

In practice:

* the token verifies who the user is  
* paid Explorer access is granted separately in 21-minute units  
* Explorer collection access is denied when the paid window is missing or expired

## **Server-side enforcement**

### **Explorer collection access is enforced on the backend.** **This means:**

* the frontend cannot unlock the full Explorer by UI flow alone  
* collection and delta routes require a valid Explorer token  
* collection and delta routes also require active Explorer entitlement  
* dataset scope is derived server-side from verified token identity

## **Demo mode**

### **Explorer also supports a demo mode.** **Current behavior:**

* demo users see a restricted partial dataset  
* demo sessions display a demo banner in the frontend  
* demo unlocks are clamped to one 21-minute unit per grant  
* the restriction is enforced server-side, not only in the UI

## **Public sharing distinction**

### **The Explorer itself is gated, but individual challenge pages remain public through:**

* /api/v1/challenges/:id  
* the public challenge page

---

## **Product Impact**

The Explorer strengthens the core loop:

##### visibility → decision → spending → impact

It ensures that:

* the system remains readable

* user actions are informed

* influence is intentional rather than random


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/game-master-admin.md =====

# **Game Master / Admin**
## **Purpose**

This layer gives the streamer and future privileged operators direct control over the live system when normal player-facing flows are not sufficient.

## **Control scope** 

Privileged control can include:

* monitoring global game state

* checking operational clocks and system status

* inspecting economy-wide metrics

* forcing or correcting certain game-state actions when needed

* supporting privileged intervention when needed

## **Role in the product** 

* This layer ensures the product remains operable in real conditions.

* It supports moderation, state correction, debugging, and manual intervention where automation or player actions alone are not sufficient.

## **Product impact** 

This feature ensures that:

* the system can be supervised during live operation

* privileged actions remain clearly separated from normal player actions

* the product can remain stable even when exceptional intervention is required


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/identity-system.md =====

# **Identity System (Unified User)**
This section explains what unified identity means from the user’s point of view inside the product.

## **Purpose**

The Identity System ensures that each user is recognized as a single entity across all interaction channels.

It allows the system to track participation, history, and influence consistently, regardless of where the user interacts.

---

## **What it does**

The system resolves user activity from multiple platforms into one persistent identity.

This includes:

* livestream platforms (e.g. chat interactions)

* Discord interactions

* web interfaces (Explorer, submission, etc.)

All actions are linked to a single internal user profile.

---

## **How it works**
The product treats one person as one persistent DMG identity, even when they interact through different channels or linked platform accounts.

This allows:

* actions from different platforms to be aggregated

* a unified history of participation

* consistent tracking of NUMBERS and activity

---

## **Aggregated influence**

A user’s NUMBERS and participation remain part of the same system identity across platforms.

This means:

* NUMBERS earned or spent through one linked platform remain meaningful across the product  
* influence is not lost when the user changes platform or access channel  
* the system treats participation as continuous rather than platform-isolated

---

## **Persistent history**

User history remains attached to the same identity over time.

This includes:

* participation history  
* progression  
* challenge-related activity  
* long-term presence in the system

### **Purpose in the system**

This ensures that cross-platform participation is not only technically linked, but also meaningful from the user’s point of view.

---

## **Account Linking Dynamics**

Users can choose how their identities behave across platforms.

### **Linked strategy**

Multiple platform accounts are merged into one user identity.

This results in:

* shared NUMBERS balance  
* unified history and progression  
* cumulative cost scaling across all linked accounts

### **Independent strategy**

Each platform account is treated as a separate user.

This results in:

* separate NUMBERS balances  
* independent cost scaling per account  
* ability to perform actions at base cost separately on each account

### **Trade-off**

* Linked → stronger progression, higher cost scaling  
* Independent → lower cost per action, fragmented progression

### **Managerial balance**

Users can structure their identities strategically across platforms, but the streamer keeps final authority over challenge execution. This prevents account strategy alone from determining outcomes and ensures that execution still depends on broader product judgment, not only on cost optimization.

### **Strategic trade-off**

This creates a strategic layer where users can trade unified perks and progression for the ability to manage balances and cost scaling separately on each platform.

---

## **Role in the system**

The Identity System connects all parts of the product.

It ensures that:

* user actions are attributed correctly

* influence is accumulated consistently

* the product behaves as a single continuous environment

Without it, interactions would remain fragmented across platforms.

---

## **Product impact**

This feature enables:

* cross-platform continuity

* continuous user progression across platforms

* a unified experience across live and offline interactions

It organizes participation across channels into a single, coherent system.

===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/numbers-system.md =====

# **NUMBERS System (Economy Layer)**
## **Purpose**

NUMBERS is the core system currency.

It allows users to interact with the product by converting engagement into measurable influence.

---

## **What users can do**

Users can use NUMBERS to:

* submit challenges

* promote challenges (push)

* access specific features (e.g. Explorer)

* interact with system mechanics (e.g. digout, auction participation)

NUMBERS is required for all meaningful actions within the system.

---

## **How it works**

NUMBERS is obtained through participation rewards and financial contribution.

It can then be spent to perform actions that influence the system.

Each action has a defined cost, creating a direct relationship between:

participation → NUMBERS → action → system impact

---

## **NUMBERS Earning Mechanics**
### **Financial support**

Users can gain NUMBERS through:

* donations  
* subscriptions  
* higher support tiers, which improve NUMBERS acquisition efficiency

### **Participation rewards**

Users can also gain NUMBERS through:

* watch time on supported platforms (currently designed as \+21 NUMBERS every 21 minutes)  
* chat activity  
* poll participation  
* leaderboard rewards  
* milestone rewards  
* temporary boosts or special reward periods

### **Design logic**

This system is designed so that influence can grow through:

* direct financial contribution  
* sustained participation over time

It supports a product where users are not limited to one path of progression.

---

## **NUMBERS Spending Mechanics**
Users can spend NUMBERS on multiple types of actions.

### **Core spending actions**

* submit a challenge  
* promote a challenge  
* revive an archived challenge  
* participate in auction mechanics  
* access protected tools such as the Explorer

### **Extended spending possibilities**
The system can also support additional spending uses such as:

* disrupt mechanics (currently implemented as a placeholder action with tracked cost and metrics)  
* livestream interactions  
* rewards, raffles, or collectibles  
* other participation-based unlocks

### **Role in the system**

This ensures that NUMBERS is not only earned, but actively used to shape behavior, prioritization, and access.

---

## **Economic logic**

NUMBERS is not only a reward currency. It is the system layer that turns participation into strategic action.

The system is designed to regulate how influence is distributed.

Key principles:

* actions require spending NUMBERS

* costs can increase based on user behavior

* different actions have different cost structures

This ensures that:

* influence is not free

* user decisions carry weight

* the system remains balanced over time

---

## **Quadratic Logic Rules**
The system uses two distinct quadratic cost rules.

### **Challenge submission**
* submission cost increases based on how many challenges the same user has already submitted that day  
* this submission cost resets daily at 21:00 UTC

### **Challenge promotion (push)**

* push cost increases only for the same user on the same challenge  
* this push cost does not reset  
* the rule is per-user, per-challenge, never-resets

### **Purpose in the system**

This separates:

* short-term submission pressure  
* long-term promotion strategy

It prevents spam, limits single-user domination, and forces more deliberate spending of NUMBERS across the system.

---

## **Live interaction discount**
When the stream is live, paid actions receive a temporary 21% discount.

### **Purpose**

* reward live participation  
* concentrate activity during live sessions  
* make real-time interaction more attractive than delayed action

---

## Community Chest / Collective Rewards
The Community Chest is a shared reward pool built from supporter contributions, forfeited challenge-removal value, or other future directed contributions.

### **What it enables**

* pooled rewards  
* community raffles  
* delayed redistribution  
* surprise unlocks or shared events

### **Purpose in the system**

This creates a collective layer of participation where generosity and coordination become part of the product experience.

---

## **Role in the system**

The NUMBERS system connects all features.

It enables:

* challenge submission

* challenge promotion

* access control

* advanced mechanics (auction, digout)

It makes all user actions trackable and comparable within the system.

## **Product impact**

This feature ensures that:

* user actions have measurable impact

* influence from multiple users can be combined on the same challenge  

* outcomes are driven by how users spend their NUMBERS

It is the foundation of the game’s economy and interaction model.

===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/onboarding-first-entry.md =====

# **Onboarding / First Entry**
## **Purpose**

DMG is designed to minimize onboarding friction.

Users do not begin through a traditional signup flow, account creation page, or password-based website account.

## **How onboarding works**

The first entry point is a chat command.

When a user sends a supported command through a connected platform:

* the backend receives the external identity context  
* the system resolves the corresponding internal DMG user or creates it if it does not yet exist  
* the action is then processed under that authenticated identity

## **What this means**

Onboarding is embedded directly into participation.

A user can enter the system simply by interacting with it.

## **Why this matters**

The first command acts as the practical entry point into the system, because it triggers identity resolution or account creation without requiring a traditional signup flow.

This design:

* removes the need for separate account creation before participation  
* reduces friction at first contact  
* keeps identity tied to the platform where the interaction originated  
* makes the bot / command layer function as the practical entry point into the product


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/promotion-push.md =====

# **Promotion System (Push)**
## **Purpose**

The Promotion system allows users to express preference and influence which challenges should be prioritized for execution.

It is the primary mechanism through which the community expresses priority and drives outcomes.

---

## **What users can do**

Users can:

* support challenges by spending NUMBERS

* increase a challenge’s priority within the system

* contribute to collective decision-making

---

## **How it works**

Each promotion (“push”) adds more NUMBERS to a challenge’s total support.

* challenges are ranked based on accumulated support, which determines eligibility for execution

* higher-supported challenges gain higher priority within the ranked pool

* eligible challenges then compete for limited execution slots

* multiple users can contribute to the same challenge

This creates a shared prioritization layer across all active challenges.

---

## **Ranking – Eligibility – Execution**
Challenges are first ranked by total NUMBERS support. Only the 21 highest-ranked challenges enter the eligible execution pool.

#### **This creates two levels:**

* ranking (all challenges compete)  
* eligibility (only the 21 highest-ranked challenges can enter the execution pool)

#### **Role in the system**

* This layer filters which challenges can realistically be executed.

#### **It ensures that:**

* execution is not based on visibility alone  
* only sufficiently supported challenges compete for limited execution time

#### **Product impact**

This system ensures that:

* community consensus determines which challenges reach execution  
* low-supported challenges do not compete equally with high-supported ones  
* promotion has a threshold effect, not just a linear effect

---

## **Challenge Selection Process**
Promotion determines rank and eligibility, but it does not guarantee automatic execution.

**This means:**

* challenges first compete for rank through community support

* only eligible challenges move into the eligible execution pool

* final execution selection is still performed by the streamer ("21")

**Final selection can happen:**

* individually by the streamer

* with community input

* through stronger community-driven scheduling over time

This ensures that promotion shapes execution priority without removing final human selection control.

---

## **Cost logic**

The system uses a dynamic cost model:

* each additional push by the same user on the same challenge becomes more expensive

* the rule applies per user and per challenge

This encourages:

* distribution of influence across multiple challenges

* strategic decision-making

* collaboration instead of domination

---

## **Confirmation flow**
Pushes follow a two-stage flow:

* quote generation  
* quote confirmation

This means:

* the system calculates the cost first  
* the user sees the quoted cost before payment  
* the quote remains valid for 30 seconds  
* the push is only applied after confirmation

Purpose in the system:

* makes the quadratic cost visible before commitment  
* reduces accidental spending  
* keeps high-cost promotion actions deliberate

---

## **Role in the system**

The Promotion system transforms user intent into measurable impact.

It creates:

* competition between challenges

* collective prioritization before final execution selection

* a direct connection between user actions, challenge ranking, and limited execution capacity

---

## **Product impact**

This feature ensures that:

* the community actively shapes what gets executed

* users influence outcomes through their pushes, with impact depending on how they distribute their NUMBERS across challenges

* outcomes are driven by the combined actions of multiple users rather than a single individual

===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/share-system.md =====

# **Share System**
## **Purpose**

The Share System allows individual challenges to be shared and turns challenge pages into entry points back into the product.

## **What users can do**

Users can

* copy or share a public link to a challenge page

* use a challenge page as a gateway toward the most relevant participation channel

## **Shared object**

The system shares the public challenge page, rather than the gated Explorer view.

This ensures that shared links remain readable and accessible outside the gated Explorer flow.

## **Contextual CTA logic**

The challenge page adapts its main call to action based on stream state:

* if the stream is live, the CTA directs users toward the live stream  
* if the stream is offline, the CTA directs users toward the main community channel (currently Discord)

## **Role in the product**

This system connects:

* challenge visibility  
* user acquisition  
* re-entry into the product loop

It allows one challenge to function both as content and as a distribution point.

## **Product impact**

This feature ensures that:

* individual challenges can be shared while still bringing users back into the product  
* challenge sharing contributes to discovery and return traffic  
* the product can redirect attention toward the most relevant participation channel depending on context


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/slots.md =====

# **Slots**
# **Scheduling / Execution Slots**

## **Purpose**

This system defines how limited stream time is turned into executable challenge time.

## **Core principle**

Execution capacity is limited.

Challenges do not move directly from promotion to execution. They must still pass through ranking, selection, and execution-capacity constraints.

They compete for a finite number of execution slots.

For the prioritization side of this process, see the Promotion (Push) section.

---

## **Execution slots**
An execution slot is a predefined 21-minute block reserved for challenge execution.

**These slots:**

* represent the available execution time in a stream.  
* define how much challenge work can actually be performed  
* create a real scheduling constraint inside the product

**Example**

* A stream might be scheduled with 9 execution slots:  
* 9 × 21-minute sessions \= 189 minutes of challenge execution time (3 hours and 9 minutes), excluding breaks or pauses.

### **Scheduling flexibility**

Slot count can vary from one stream session to another depending on available time and stream conditions. Execution slots can be planned by the streamer and may later incorporate stronger community involvement in scheduling.

## **Prioritization logic**

Execution slots define capacity, not priority.

Priority is determined upstream through the Promotion (Push) system.

---

## **Role in the system**

This is where final challenge selection becomes concrete, because eligible challenges must still fit into the limited execution capacity of the stream.

Execution slots connect:

* challenge promotion  
* challenge selection  
* real creator time

They make limited time visible and actionable.

## **Product impact**

This system ensures that:

* stream time is treated as a finite resource  
* promotion has concrete scheduling consequences  
* challenges compete for actual execution capacity, not only visibility


===== FILE: dmg-doc/features/tiers-access-structure.md =====

# **Tiers and Access Structure**
## **Purpose**

The product includes a progression system that rewards different levels of participation and support without removing the core experience from less involved users.

## **Tier philosophy**

The system is designed so that:

\- all users can influence the product

\- deeper involvement unlocks additional perks

\- progression can come from activity, spending, or financial support

## **Tier groups**

### **Base tier**

All users start here and can access the core participation loop.

### **Engaged tier**

Users unlock additional benefits through NUMBERS spending and sustained activity.

### **Supporter tier**

Users who financially support the project gain stronger perks, recognition, and deeper access.

### **Top supporter layer**

Short-term leaderboards reward standout contribution over daily, weekly, or monthly periods.

## **Purpose in the system**

This structure creates:

* progression without hard restriction  
* stronger incentives for sustained participation  
* multiple ways to deepen involvement in the product

---

## **Subscriber Perks**

Financial support can unlock additional benefits beyond basic participation.

### **Examples include:**

* daily NUMBERS reward  
* discounts on game commands  
* reserved challenge slots  
* access to deeper participation features (e.g. exclusive game commands)  
* exclusive raffles

### **Purpose in the system**

These perks strengthen retention, reward sustained support, and connect financial support to deeper participation.


===== FILE: dmg-doc/overview.md =====

# **Product Overview: Drummer Manager Game.**
### **60s pitch.**

DMG is a gamified livestream system where audiences actively influence what a creator does next.

Users submit challenges, support the ones they want to see happen, and compete or collaborate to decide how limited stream time is used.

Instead of passive viewing, the system turns engagement into structured influence through a shared decision layer.

The result is a livestream experience where the audience helps shape the work, not just watch it.

### **1 sentence pitch.**

Drummer Manager Game is a gamified livestream system where viewers use a shared currency to influence how a streamer’s limited time is spent by submitting and promoting challenges.

---

## **Introduction.**

**Drummer Manager Game** is a community-driven livestream product where the audience helps decide what happens next.

Instead of staying passive, viewers can submit ideas, promote the ones they support, and influence how the streamer’s time is used. The system is built around **NUMBERS**, the product’s core currency, which turns engagement into influence.

The goal is to make the creative process visible, interactive, and continuously evolving over time. The community does not only watch the result – it helps shape the work behind it.

---

## **Core Concepts and Product Principle**

The audience helps shape what happens next, how work is prioritized, and how the experience evolves over time.

### **This means:**

* participation is structured rather than passive  
* the product turns input into visible consequences over time  
* actions should be meaningful, strategic, and visible  
* the audience is not limited to watching outcomes

This creates a product where the community helps shape priorities and outcomes over time, rather than only watching the result.

---

## **Core Product Idea**

DMG turns the audience into an **active management layer**.

Users submit challenges and promote (push) the ones they want to see happen. This helps determine what gets priority, while the streamer keeps final execution control.

This makes the product feel less like a standard stream and more like a shared creative system.

---

## **Core Commands Principle**

The main interaction layer is built around simple chat commands.

### **Purpose**

This keeps the system:

* fast to use

* easy to understand

* accessible during live and offline participation

### **Role in the system**

Commands are the main interface between users and the system.

They also act as the practical onboarding path, because users can enter the product through interaction rather than through a traditional website account flow.

---

## **How It Works**

The product revolves around **Challenges**.

A Challenge is a task, objective, or direction the community wants the streamer to tackle. Challenges can be technical, creative, playful, short, or recurring.

Once submitted, challenges enter the system and can be promoted by the community. The more support a challenge gets, the more visible it becomes. This increases its chances of being selected for execution within the limited execution time available during streams.

Because the streamer’s time is limited, not everything can be executed. That limitation is part of the product: the community is effectively deciding how the streamer’s limited time gets used, through both competition and collective support.

---

## **Live and offline continuity**

The system operates both during livestream sessions and outside of them.

This allows:

* real-time interaction during live sessions  
* continued participation between streams  
* a product loop that remains active over time instead of stopping when the stream ends

---

## **NUMBERS**

**NUMBERS** is the product’s core currency. It gives users a way to act inside the system. NUMBERS can be spent to:

* submit challenges  
* promote challenges  
* revive archived challenges  
* access tools such as the Explorer

This creates a simple loop: **engagement → value → influence → impact**

NUMBERS is not an extra reward layer. It is one of the product’s core systems.

---

## **Tiers and Progression**

The product includes a tiered engagement system that rewards participation and support.

All users start with access to the core experience and can increase their influence through activity, NUMBERS usage, or financial support.

Higher engagement unlocks additional perks such as:

* more influence over the system  
* access to exclusive interactions  
* more visibility and recognition

The goal is not to restrict access, but to create a progression system where continued involvement leads to deeper impact.

---

## **Quadratic Logic**
To keep the system fair, repeated actions become more expensive.

* **Submitting multiple challenges** increases cost.  
* **Repeatedly pushing (promoting) the same challenge** increases cost.

This prevents spam, limits domination by a single user, and encourages strategic thinking. This encourages more deliberate decisions instead of repetitive behavior.

---

## **Challenge Lifecycle**

Challenges move through a structured lifecycle. They can be:

* **Active**  
* **In Progress**  
* **Completed**  
* **Failed**  
* **Archived**  
* **Auctioned**  
* **Removed**  
* **Under Review**

This gives the system memory. Challenges build history, momentum, and outcomes over time instead of disappearing.

---

## **Time Structure**
The product uses a simple time structure built around the number 21.

* **21-minute session** \= base execution unit  
* **21-day window** \= standard challenge lifespan

This structure keeps the system consistent, memorable, and easy to recognize across the experience.

---

## **Community Role**

The audience is an active part of the product. **Users can:**

* submit ideas  
* promote the challenges they want to see executed  
* track progress  
* revive past challenges  
* influence direction over time

The system creates **structured influence**, but not total control.

---

## **Managerial Override**

The community influences priority, but final execution control remains with the streamer. This means **the streamer can**:

* choose which eligible challenges are actually executed

* pause or stop a challenge if needed

* balance community demand with physical condition, stream constraints, and long-term project needs

### **Purpose in the system**

This keeps the product collaborative without removing human control over execution.

---

## **Product Identity**

DMG combines a strong symbolic identity with a clear structural logic. The number 21 is both an identity marker and a recurring product rule used across the experience.

**It appears in**

* timing, 

* pricing, 

* rewards, 

* system structure

This gives the product a recognizable identity and a consistent internal logic.

---

## **Why It Matters**

Drummer Manager Game turns engagement into structured influence.

Instead of only watching or donating, users interact with a system where their actions matter and have visible consequences. This creates:

* stronger engagement

* clearer progression

* a more memorable experience

---

## **Operating Commitment**

The product depends on a consistent livestream rhythm to remain meaningful over time. 

It works best when the experience includes:

* regular live presence

* enough live time for challenges to be executed and followed over time

### **Purpose in the system**

A consistent cadence makes participation credible, strengthens community trust, and gives the system enough continuity to matter over time.

---

## **Community Strategy and Expansion**

The product is not tied to a single platform. It can operate across livestream platforms for real-time participation and community channels for continued participation outside live sessions.

### **Current model**

* livestream platforms support real-time participation

* Discord acts as the main community hub outside live sessions

* the same participation rules can be extended to other compatible channels over time

**As participation grows, the product can reinforce that growth through:**

* reminders that viewers can influence what happens next

* features that highlight notable ideas, moments, or challenge momentum  
* safeguards such as cost escalation, gated access, and rate limits to keep growth from degrading interaction quality

### **Purpose in the product**

This helps audience growth strengthen product participation, instead of evolving separately from it.

---

## **In One Sentence**

**Drummer Manager Game** is a gamified livestream product where the community uses **NUMBERS** to submit, promote, and shape challenges, turning audience engagement into structured influence over the creative process.

# System Architecture

===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/api-structure.md =====

# **API STRUCTURE**
The API is organized into endpoint groups. Each group has a specific role in the product.

---

## **PUBLIC API (READ-ONLY)**

### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/challenges/:id`

### **Role**

This endpoint exposes one public challenge record for the public challenge page.

No Explorer token is required.

### **Notes**

* `/api/v1/challenges/:id` returns one challenge for the public challenge page.  
* This route remains openly shareable outside the Explorer flow.

### **Core principle**

This route is public, read-only, and safe to expose without Explorer authentication.

---

## **EXPLORER DATA API**
### **Endpoints**

* `` `/api/v1/challenges` ``  
* `` `/api/v1/challenges/delta` ``

### **Role**

These endpoints expose Explorer challenge data for authenticated Explorer sessions.

### **Access model**

* Explorer token required  
* Explorer paid entitlement required  
* dataset scope derived server-side from verified token identity  
* demo users receive the restricted dataset  
* full users receive the full dataset

### **Notes**

* `/api/v1/challenges` returns the Explorer collection feed  
* `/api/v1/challenges/delta` returns incremental Explorer updates  
* frontend sends Bearer auth for both endpoints  
* these routes are read-only but not public

---

## **COMMAND API**

Base path: \``` /api/v1/command` ``

### **Role**

This route family handles external user command ingress.  
It receives command payloads from chat-connected systems and routes them into the backend command-processing layer after authentication and rate limiting.

### **Typical responsibilities**

* receive command payloads from external bot / loyalty systems

* authenticate and resolve the acting user

* apply rate limiting before command execution

* forward commands into the centralized command dispatcher

---

## **TOKEN / ACCESS API**

### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/token/verify-challengesubmitform`  
* `/api/v1/token/verify-explorer`  
* `/api/v1/token/grant-explorer-access`

### **Role**

These endpoints handle identity verification and gated web-feature access. They are used for:

* secure access to the challenge submit form  
* gated access to the Explorer  
* paid Explorer access grant / extension

### **Notes**

* `/api/v1/token/verify-challengesubmitform` verifies the token received from chat, resolves the user identity, and returns the submit-form context. This includes:  
  * username  
  * platform  
  * daily submission count  
  * server-calculated base cost  
* `/api/v1/token/verify-explorer` verifies identity and returns current Explorer access state. This includes:  
  * username  
  * platform  
  * current access validity  
  * remaining Explorer minutes  
  * merit pricing eligibility  
  * demo/full identity scope

* `/api/v1/token/grant-explorer-access` verifies identity, deducts NUMBERS, and grants or extends Explorer access. This includes:

  * paid access window creation / extension

  * merit-based price calculation

  * demo unlock clamping to one unit

  * granted minutes and remaining minutes in response

### **Core principle**

These routes separate three concerns:

* authentication

* access-state verification

* paid entitlement grant

---

## **USER ACTION API**

### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/user/*`

### **Role**

These endpoints handle direct game actions initiated by a player. This includes:

* challenge submission  
* web form challenge submission  
* push quote  
* push confirm  
* digout  
* disrupt  
* challenge removal

### **Notes**

This route group is player-facing game control. It is not admin control. It exists to let a verified user perform actions that affect:

* their own balance  
* their own challenge actions  
* the shared challenge system

### **Important distinction**

User routes are not just generic “control” routes. They are the normal gameplay action layer for players.

### **Examples**

* A player submits a challenge  
* A player pushes a challenge  
* A player revives an archived challenge  
* A player removes their own challenge under allowed rules

---

## **GAME MASTER / PRIVILEGED CONTROL API**
### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/gamemaster/*`

### **Role**

These endpoints handle privileged control over the game state. This includes:

* executing a challenge manually  
* forcing a challenge status  
* other low-level control actions reserved for privileged roles

### **Notes**

This route group is different from normal player actions. It is used for:

* the streamer  
* future moderators or privileged operators  
* special roles that need deeper control over the system

### **Important distinction**

* **User routes** \= normal player actions  
* **GM routes** \= privileged control over the system itself

---

## **STREAM API**

### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/stream/live`  
* `/api/v1/stream/offline`  
* `/api/v1/stream/stats`

### **Role**

These endpoints handle stream state changes and stream status retrieval. They are used for:

* detecting when the stream goes live  
* detecting when the stream goes offline  
* providing current stream status to the website

### **Notes**

* `/api/v1/stream/live` processes the live event  
* `/api/v1/stream/offline` processes the offline event  
* `/api/v1/stream/stats` returns current stream status and global stream stats

---

## **REFERENCE / SUBMISSION UX API**
### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/references/title`

### **Role**

This endpoint improves the challenge submission experience. It is used to fetch the title of a reference URL when the user pastes a link into the submit form.

### **Notes**

The goal is to reduce friction during challenge submission. Instead of asking the user to manually fill every reference title, the system tries to resolve it automatically. Supported sources currently include:

* YouTube  
* Vimeo  
* SoundCloud  
* Spotify  
* Wikipedia  
* generic public pages

### **Core principle**

This route is not part of the game logic itself. It is a submission UX helper.

---

## **ADMIN / SYSTEM MONITORING API**

### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/admin/pulse`

### **Role**

This endpoint is used for internal system monitoring. It provides a quick overview of:

* system health  
* database / Redis availability  
* global economy totals  
* maintenance state  
* global counters

### **Notes**

This route is protected by an admin secret. It is not a public product endpoint. It exists to monitor the operational state of the system, not to support player-facing gameplay.

---

## **CLOCK / MAINTENANCE API**
### **Endpoints**

* `/api/v1/clock/run-daily-maintenance`

### **Role**

This endpoint is used to trigger daily maintenance safely. It handles recurring system maintenance tasks that should not be run manually without authorization.

### **Notes**

This route is protected by a cron secret. It is an internal operational endpoint. It belongs to the maintenance layer, not the gameplay layer.

Daily maintenance is tied to the system’s UTC-based daily reset logic and should execute in alignment with that schedule.

---

## **CORE SEPARATION**

The API follows a strict separation of responsibilities.

* **Public API**: Read-only challenge data  
* **Command API:** external user command ingress, identity resolution, and routing into the backend command-processing layer.  
* **Token / Access API**: Identity verification and access control for protected web tools  
* **User Action API**: Normal player actions that affect gameplay  
* **Game Master / Privileged Control API**: Privileged control over the game state  
* **Stream API**: Live / offline events and stream status  
* **Reference / Submission UX API**: Submission quality-of-life helpers  
* **Admin / System Monitoring API**: System health and economy monitoring  
* **Clock / Maintenance API**: Protected maintenance execution

---

## **WHY THIS MATTERS**

This separation keeps the product easier to understand, safer to maintain, and easier to scale. It also makes the boundary very clear between:

* public browsing  
* player actions  
* privileged control  
* stream state  
* maintenance  
* internal monitoring.

===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/backend-architecture.md =====

# **Backend Architecture**
## **Overview**

The backend is responsible for managing the game logic, enforcing rules, and synchronizing all player interactions. It acts as the central system coordinating:

* challenge lifecycle

* NUMBERS transactions

* time progression

* identity resolution

* stream state

The backend is designed to apply rules consistently and stay synchronized with external systems and integrations.

---

## **Core Systems**

### **Challenge System**
Handles the full lifecycle of challenges. Responsibilities:

* creation (submission flow)

* promotion (push logic)

* execution state

* expiration (21-day logic)

* revival (digout mechanic)

* removal and refunds

This system ensures challenges evolve consistently over time.

### **NUMBERS & Transaction System**

Handles all spending and validation of NUMBERS. **Responsibilities**:

* cost calculation (quadratic logic)

* balance checks and transaction authorization

* synchronization with Lumia (source of truth)

* atomic transaction handling to avoid partial updates when a payment or write fails

This system ensures NUMBERS spending stays synchronized, validated, and safe across both local game state and external balance updates.

### **Time & Session System**

Controls how time affects the game. **Responsibilities**:

* 21-minute session execution

* daily resets (submission counters and daily time-based rules)

* 21-day challenge lifespan tracking

* recurring challenge cadence enforcement

This system applies time-based rules automatically so progression, resets, and challenge state changes do not depend on manual intervention.

### **Stream State System**
Tracks whether the stream is live or offline. **Responsibilities**:

* live / offline state

* recovery of the current stream-day state after restart

* protection against counting the same calendar day twice

* live-state-dependent behavior such as command discounts and other engagement rules

This state directly affects pricing, engagement, and user behavior.

### **Identity & Access System**

Resolves users and secures actions. **Responsibilities**:

* platform identity resolution

* token verification

* linking multiple accounts

* protecting web actions through token-based identity checks

This allows a user to interact seamlessly across platforms while maintaining a single identity.

### **Event & Notification System**

Handles system feedback and real-time updates. **Responsibilities**:

* logging

* system events

* notifications across chat, UI, and real-time client updates 

This ensures the system remains observable and interactive.

## **Brand & Design Principles**
The backend follows a few core principles:

* Single source of truth for NUMBERS balances (Lumia)

* Rules are applied consistently

* No silent failures

* Automation over manual control

* Cross-platform consistency

---

## **Automation Principle**
The product is designed to automate as much system logic as possible.

This includes:

* challenge validation and processing  
* ranking and eligibility updates  
* session and time-based progression  
* transaction handling  
* system feedback and synchronization

### **Purpose in the system**

This reduces manual overhead (fewer manual checks during live interaction), improves consistency (the same rules apply every time), and helps the system scale as participation grows.

# **Brand / Design Principles**

# **Brand / Design Principles**

## **Foundation**

* authenticity, with a slightly sarcastic edge

* transparent and accessible participation

* a product that feels interactive, readable, and active

## **Visual style**

* organized density rather than stripped-down minimalism

===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/challenge-lifecycle-system.md =====

# **Challenge Lifecycle System**
## **Overview**

The Challenge Lifecycle defines how a challenge evolves over time. It defines the states a challenge can move through, from creation to completion, removal, or archival. This system is central to the product because it drives:

* gameplay progression

* user decisions

* economic flow

---

## **Core Principle**

A challenge is not static. It moves through a sequence of states based on:

* time

* user actions

* system logic

---

## **Time & Execution Model**

Challenges evolve over time based on a structured time system.

#### **Session unit: 21 minutes**

base execution unit

#### **Duration types:**
* ONE\_OFF → **must be** **completed** within a **single stream day**, across one or multiple 21-minute sessions

* RECURRING → executed across multiple sessions following a **defined cadence** over time

#### **Cadence (for RECURRING challenges)**
Defines how sessions are scheduled over time (e.g. daily, weekly, monthly, or custom intervals)

Recurring challenges require more than multiple sessions. They also require those sessions to happen at the required pace.

**This means:**

* a recurring challenge defines a cadence window

* the system tracks how many sessions were completed within that window

* if the required count is reached, the cadence window resets

* if the required count is not reached in time, the challenge fails

This makes pacing part of the challenge’s success conditions and distinguishes RECURRING execution from simple ONE\_OFF multi-session completion.

#### **Challenge lifespan: 21 days**
active period before archival if not executed

#### **Commitment window**

The 21-day lifespan starts when a challenge is submitted to the system.

If the challenge does not gain enough promotion within that window, it moves

to Archived.

#### **Stream Day Logic**

A challenge’s active lifespan is measured through Stream Days rather than simple calendar time.

This means:

* one Stream Day is counted when at least one session is executed

* the 21-day active period is measured in Stream Days

* archival depends on Stream Days, not Real Days

This system defines how challenges evolve over time and how execution is distributed across sessions.

---

## **Main States**
A challenge can exist in one of the following states:

* **Active**: The challenge is live and can receive interactions. This includes:

  * pushes

  * disruptions

  * auction contributions (when applicable)

* **In Progress**: The challenge has started execution but has not yet completed all of its required sessions.

  * Important: “In Progress” does not mean the challenge is necessarily being played right now. The real-time execution state is tracked separately through the isExecuting flag.

* **Completed**: All required sessions for the challenge have been completed.

* **Failed**: The challenge started execution but did not meet its execution requirements or cadence rules.

* **Archived**: The challenge is no longer active, is no longer eligible for normal progression, and is kept in system history.

* **Removed**: The challenge was manually removed from the system. This can trigger:

  * refunds

  * redistribution of value

* **Under Review****:** The challenge is in a review-sensitive state before normal lifecycle handling is fully confirmed.

* **Auctioned**: The challenge has been placed into an auction state by the streamer and assigned a NUMBERS threshold.

  * If the community reaches that threshold, the challenge is immediately selected for execution regardless of its normal ranking.

  * If the threshold is not reached, the challenge can move to Archived according to the auction outcome rules.

---

## **State Transitions**

Challenges move between states through:

* **Time**

  * expiration (e.g. 21 Stream Day day limit)

  * execution scheduling

* **User Actions**

  * pushing a challenge

  * removing a challenge

  * reviving a challenge (digout)

  * participating in an auction by contributing toward the NUMBERS threshold

* **System Events**

  * session tick (21-minute session completion)

  * session completion updates

  * daily maintenance (e.g. archival checks)

  * stream state (live / offline) changes affecting execution flow

---

## **State Transition Mental Model**

A challenge follows a simple progression model:

| Under Review → Active → (optional Auctioned) → In Progress → Final State |
| :---- |

In practice, that means:

**Under Review**: The challenge is waiting for validation or decision.

**Active**: The challenge is live in the system and can receive community interaction.

**Auctioned**: The challenge has been assigned a threshold-based execution condition.

**In Progress**: The challenge has started execution but still has remaining sessions to complete.

**Completed / Failed / Removed / Archived**: The challenge exits active progression and becomes part of system history, with the possibility of revival in specific cases. 

This model is important because it separates three distinct layers:

* availability in the system

* execution progress

* final resolution

It also makes clear that:

* a challenge can be active without being executed yet

* a challenge can be in progress without being executed at this exact moment

* a challenge only becomes completed when all required sessions have been successfully completed.

---

## **Economic Impact**

Each state transition can affect the system economy. **Examples**:

* **pushing** → increases challenge value  
* **removal** → triggers partial refunds and redistribution  
* **completion →** ends the challenge as an active progression object

---

## **Lifecycle Importance**

The lifecycle system ensures:

* challenges remain dynamic

* users can influence outcomes

* the system continuously evolves

It transforms challenges from static entries into active game elements.

---

## **Relationship with Other Systems**

This system interacts with:

* backend challenge logic  
* clock / maintenance logic  
* stream state logic  
* NUMBERS and transaction system  
* Game Master control logic

## **Why This Matters**

The Challenge Lifecycle is the core game loop. It defines:

* how users interact with the system

* how value moves

* how the game progresses over time

Without it, the product would be a static database instead of a dynamic system.


===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/frontend-architecture.md =====

# **Frontend Architecture**
## **Overview**

The frontend is organized as a set of dedicated pages connected by a shared visual and interaction system. The goal is to keep each page focused on one role while maintaining a consistent brand, layout logic, and user experience across the whole website. The frontend is not a single application in the framework sense. It is a modular multi-page website built around shared components, styling, and UX rules.

---

## **Shared Frontend Principles**

The frontend follows a few core principles across pages:

* **Consistent branding:** The same visual identity is reused across the website through shared typography, shared colors, shared spacing logic, and repeated structural patterns.  
* **Shared container logic:** The main pages are built around a primary content container with animated neon borders. This creates a recognizable visual shell and keeps the experience coherent from page to page.  
* **Shared typography:**  
  * **DM Sans** is used for strong titles, major headings, and calls to action.  
  * **Roboto** is used for body text, labels, smaller system text, and supporting information.  
* **Shared global stylesheet****:** `global.css` acts as the base layer for the whole frontend.  
* **Shared footer visibility logic:** A persistent social footer is reused across pages to maintain visibility of the creator’s ecosystem and encourage continued engagement beyond the current page.

---

## **Core Frontend Pages**

### **1\. Landing Page**

* **Role**: The landing page is the simplest entry point into the product. It currently routes users quickly toward four main actions:  
  * Explorer Database  
  * How to Play  
  * Submit Challenge  
  * Support the Project  
* **Purpose**: This page acts as a clean entry hub rather than a content-heavy page. Its role is orientation and conversion.  
* **Notes**: It uses the shared fonts, shared visual language, and shared footer, but not the shared site header.

### **2\. Explorer Page**
* **Role**: The Explorer is the browsing interface for the challenge database. It allows users to:  
  * browse the challenge list  
  * search and filter  
  * inspect details  
  * follow challenge updates over time  
* **Data Role**: This page is the main data navigation page of the frontend. It is built for exploration, not submission.  
* **Access Logic**: The Explorer is access-gated and verifies the user before the interface becomes available.

* **Notes**: This page combines:

  * token verification

  * paid access-window verification

  * NUMBERS-based access grant

  * Bearer-authenticated data loading

  * client-side filtering and search

  * live delta polling

  * server-authoritative dataset restriction for demo/full sessions

* **Important distinction:**

  * Explorer collection browsing is gated

  * public single-challenge pages remain openly shareable

### **3\. Public Challenge Page**
* **Role**: The public challenge page displays one individual challenge. It is designed for sharing, public visibility, and focused reading of a single challenge.  
* **Purpose**: This page gives a focused view of one challenge without the extra browsing tools of the Explorer.

### **4\. Challenge Submit Form**
* **Role**: The submit form is the structured entry point for challenge creation. It guides the user through:  
  * verification  
  * challenge definition  
  * duration and cadence setup  
  * reference input  
  * submission  
  * post-submission review and sharing  
* **Purpose**: This page turns challenge creation into a controlled and readable flow.  
* **Notes**: It is one of the most refined pages in the system because it combines token verification, step-by-step UX, dynamic form logic, post-submission success state, and structured challenge review.

### **5\. FAQ Page**

* **Role**: The FAQ page explains the game in a simple, progressive way.  
* **Purpose**: It acts as a lightweight onboarding page.  
* **Notes**: It was one of the earliest pages built and is currently simpler than the main product pages. It does not yet use the full shared header system.

### **6\. Donation Page**

* **Role**: The donation page is a direct support page.  
* **Purpose**: Its function is simple: convert donation intent into action.  
* **Notes**: It is intentionally minimal and centered around the Ko-fi embed. It uses the shared visual shell and the shared footer, but not the shared site header.

### **7\. Admin / Command Center**
* **Role**: The admin page is the streamer-side dashboard.  
* **Purpose**: It provides a monitoring interface for system status, operational clocks, economy state, and global metrics.  
* **Notes**: This page is internal-facing rather than community-facing. It follows the shared visual language but serves a different operational role.

---

## **Explorer Client-Side Cache Model**

The Explorer keeps a live copy of challenge data in the browser.

The backend remains the source of truth, while the frontend stores the current challenge list locally for filtering, searching, and rendering.

**This allows:**

* fast local filtering and search  
* responsive UI updates without repeated full reloads  
* efficient synchronization through the delta updates endpoint

### **Why it matters**

This architecture prioritizes responsiveness and UI flexibility while challenge volume remains moderate.

---

## **Why the Frontend Structure Matters**

The frontend is now organized around a clear split:

* **Pages define context**  
* **Shared components, styles, and interaction rules ensure consistency**

This matters because it allows the website to scale without becoming visually fragmented. It also makes the project look more serious from a product and implementation perspective: clear roles per page, reusable components, consistent UX, and a maintainable growth path.

---

## **Current Frontend Maturity**

The most refined frontend pages today are:

* **Challenge Submit Form**  
* **Explorer**  
* **Public Challenge**

These pages already show the strongest level of architectural maturity and product consistency. Other pages already follow the same direction, even if they are still lighter or less mature: Landing Page, FAQ, Donation, and Admin. This means the frontend is no longer a collection of isolated pages. It is already becoming a **coherent product experience**.

---

## **Frontend Backlog Direction**

* **Shared audio behavior across pages**: The mute button already exists in the shared header, but audio behavior is not yet fully shared across all relevant pages.  
* **Further page harmonization**: Some lighter pages still need to be aligned more closely with the stronger structure already used by Explorer, Public Challenge, and Submit Form.  
* **FAQ clarification**: The FAQ exists as an early onboarding page but still needs future refinement to better match the maturity of the rest of the frontend.

---

## **Conclusion**

**The frontend architecture is built around one key idea: Different pages, one product feel.**

This is achieved through:

* shared branding

* consistent page structure

* unified user experience

That makes the frontend easier to maintain, easier to scale, and much more professional to present.


===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/interaction-pace-model.md =====

# **Interaction Pace Model**
## **Overview**

The system operates across two interaction modes depending on whether the stream is live or offline.

## **Live Mode (Stream Online)**

* Interaction happens in real time through livestream platforms  
* Actions (push, submission, etc.) are immediate and visible  
* The system concentrates interaction on live participation when the stream is online

## **Offline Mode (Stream Offline)**

* Interaction continues asynchronously through community channels such as Discord  
* Users can still submit, promote, and interact with challenges  
* The system remains active even without a live stream

## **Mode Switching**

* The system automatically switches behavior based on stream state  
* Some interaction channels may be limited during live sessions so participation stays concentrated on the stream

## **Role in the System**

This model ensures that:

* the participation model continues outside live streams  
* engagement exists both in real time and over longer periods  
* user activity continues to influence the system at all times

===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/maintenance-logic.md =====

# **Maintenance Logic**
## **Overview**

Maintenance is the daily backend process that advances system time and applies rule checks that should not depend on manual intervention.

It is scheduled to run once per day at 21:00 UTC.

## **What it does**

Daily maintenance is responsible for:

* advancing the Real Day clock  
* advancing the global Stream Day clock when a stream occurred during the maintenance window  
* processing user daily tick logic  
* enforcing cadence rules for RECURRING challenges  
* archiving expired challenges when the conditions are met  
* failing unfinished ONE\_OFF challenges when the contiguity rule is broken

---

## **User daily tick logic**
During maintenance, the system updates user activity counters based on what happened since the previous maintenance point.

**This means:**

* users are checked once per Real Day  
* the system determines whether they were active during the maintenance window  
* live activity increments Stream Day-related user counters  
* non-live activity increments offline activity counters

### **Purpose in the system**

This keeps user activity history aligned with the two-clock model and preserves the distinction between live participation and offline participation.

---

## **Safety conditions**
Maintenance does not apply every rule blindly.

Some checks depend on stream conditions.

**This means:**

* cadence checks always run  
* archival and ONE\_OFF contiguity checks only run when a stream occurred during the window  
* those checks are deferred if a stream is currently live

### **Purpose in the system**

This prevents the system from failing or archiving challenges at the wrong moment, especially while a stream is still active.

---

## **Why this matters**

Maintenance is the system’s daily control layer.

**It ensures that:**

* time-based rules are enforced consistently  
* user activity counters remain accurate  
* challenge state changes happen even without manual oversight  
* daily progression stays synchronized with actual stream activity

# **Shared UI System**

* visual consistency

* reusable components

This system allows multiple pages to behave like a single product.

This avoids duplication and keeps the frontend scalable without a framework.

Defined in `global.css`. Includes:

## **Shared Interaction Components**

## **Utility Classes**

Defined in `global.css`.

**Purpose**: Provides small reusable behaviors without requiring page-specific CSS duplication.

The interface follows strict wording rules:

* avoid introducing new terms unnecessarily

* reuse existing vocabulary

* keep labels short and clear 

**Purpose**: Reduce cognitive load and make the system easier to understand.

---

## **Why This System Matters**

This shared UI system ensures:

* all pages feel like part of the same product

* shared UI changes can be made centrally

* new pages can be added without redesigning everything 

It is the foundation of frontend scalability.

**Frontend Architecture** defines: 

* pages

* roles

* navigation
