* components

* styles

* interactions

**Relationship:** Both work together, but they should remain separate in the documentation.


===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/time-session-system.md =====

# **Time & Session System**
## **Time Standard**

The system uses UTC as its reference time standard.

### **Why UTC**

* keeps the product consistent across platforms and countries  
* avoids local timezone ambiguity  
* makes daily resets and time-based rules predictable for a worldwide audience

### **Daily reset point**
* daily resets and daily clock transitions are anchored to 21:00 UTC

---

## Two-Watermark Clock System
The system tracks time using two distinct clocks with different roles.

### **Stream Days (Execution Clock)**
Counts the number of UTC calendar days in which at least one 21-minute session was executed.

Multiple sessions in the same day count as one Stream Day.

**Purpose**:

* measure actual execution effort  
* track content production over time  
* support archival rules and long-term activity tracking

### **Real Days (System Clock)**
Counts the number of calendar days since the project started.

Increments daily at 21:00 UTC.

**Purpose**:

* enforce cadence windows, daily submission resets, and other Real Day-based rules  
* provide the time reference used for recurring challenge cadence checks  
* keep Real Day progression independent from livestream activity

### **Why two clocks**

Execution and progression are not the same.

* Stream Days reflect actual work done  
* Real Days reflect system time passing

**This separation ensures that:**

* challenge archival and other progression rules tied to actual execution depend on real activity, not just time passing.  
* system mechanics remain consistent even without streams

---

## **Daily Reset Logic**

Some system rules are evaluated or refreshed every day at 21:00 UTC.

### **This includes**

* submission quadratic cost scaling  
* daily maintenance-driven user activity tracking  
* other daily maintenance rules tied to system time such as RECURRING cadence enforcement, archival checks, and ONE\_OFF contiguity checks

### **Purpose in the system**

This keeps daily submission cost escalation meaningful while giving users a predictable reset point each day.

---

## **User daily tick logic**
The system updates user activity counters during daily maintenance.

### **This means:**

* users are checked once per Real Day  
* the system determines whether they were active since the last maintenance point  
* live activity increments Stream Day-related user counters  
* non-live activity increments offline activity counters

### **Purpose in the system:**

* keeps user activity history aligned with the two-clock model  
* distinguishes live participation from offline participation over time

---

## **Recurring cadence enforcement**

For RECURRING challenges, the backend checks whether the required number of sessions was completed within the allowed cadence window.

If the requirement is met, the cadence window resets.

If it is not met in time, the challenge fails.

---

## **Stream-day recovery and duplicate-day protection**

The system protects Stream Day logic from being advanced incorrectly.  
**This means:**

* stream state can be recovered after restart

* multiple streams on the same UTC calendar day do not count as multiple Stream Days

===== FILE: dmg-doc/system-architecture/token-identity-system.md =====

# **Token / Identity System**
# **Token / Identity System**
This section explains how identity is authenticated, verified, and enforced at the system level.

## **Overview**

The Token / Identity System is responsible for securely identifying users across the product. It ensures that:

* each action is tied to a verified identity

* platform accounts are correctly mapped to users

* access to protected features is controlled

This system is used across:

* challenge submission

* explorer access

* admin interactions

* future paid access features

## **Core Principle**
The system is built on a simple idea:

**One user | Multiple platform identities | One consistent identity layer**

This allows the product to:

* unify users across platforms  
* track activity reliably  
* maintain one consistent identity layer across the product

---

## **Identity Records**

The system is structured around three main entities:

### **User**
The central identity in the system. It represents:

* a unique player

* aggregated activity

* global stats

### **Account**
Represents one platform-specific identity record linked to a user.

It includes: 

* platform name

* platform identifier

* username / display name

* platform-specific balance and activity tracking

**Purpose:** 

Store the external identity context used for authentication and user resolution.

### **Perennial Token**
A persistent authentication token stored in the database and managed by the system. **Each token is**:

* linked to a user

* linked to a specific account

* manually enabled or disabled by the system operators

**Purpose**: This enables:

* long-lived access (e.g. trusted users, admin, testing)

* bypassing JWT expiration when needed

* controlled access without re-authentication

  ---

## **How external identity becomes internal identity**
The system resolves an external platform identity into one internal DMG user identity.

**In practice:**

(`platformId` \+ `platformName`) → centralUserId

This is the core identity-resolution rule used before protected actions are processed.

Username and display name remain mutable account context, but they are not the canonical identity key.

---

## **Authentication Methods**
The system supports two authentication methods:

### **JWT Tokens**

**Used for**: standard user sessions, temporary authentication

**Properties:**

* signed using a secret

* time-limited (default: 21 minutes)

* include user and platform identity information

### **Perennial Tokens**
**Used for**: persistent access, internal tools, advanced users 

**Properties:**

* stored in database

* manually activated/deactivated

* no expiration by default

  ---

## **How Identity Is Verified**
When a token is received:

* **Step 1**: Check whether the token exists in the PerennialToken table. If valid, return the associated user and account identity.

* **Step 2**: If not found, verify it as a standard JWT.

This creates a hybrid system:

* flexible for development and power users

* secure for standard usage

### **Token Payload**
Each token contains: userId, platformId, platformName, and username.

**Purpose**: This ensures that every request carries identity context and can be processed without additional lookups.

---

## **Token Lifetime Control**

JWT tokens use controlled expiration.

* **Default**: 21 minutes  
* **Validation**: duration is sanitized and capped at a maximum defined in config.

**Purpose**: Prevents overly long sessions and unsafe token usage.

---

## **Identity in the Frontend**
The frontend uses tokens to:

* verify access to protected pages  
* display user identity (username \+ platform name)  
* personalize interactions

**Example**: Explorer and Submit Form require token verification before access and display user identity through the header component.

---

## **Link and Identity Match**

### **Purpose**

This logic ensures that protected web actions are performed by the same user who initiated the request from chat.

### **How it works**

* chat platforms remain the primary identity source  
* when a user requests access to a protected web feature from chat, the system generates a user-specific access link  
* the web action is then verified against the originating identity before any protected action is allowed

### **Why it matters**

* improves security by tying protected actions to the same verified identity that requested the link  
* keeps the access flow fast and usable by avoiding separate website accounts and passwords  
* prevents NUMBERS spending from being applied to the wrong platform account

### **Important note**

Private links should be treated like temporary login links, not like harmless share links. Anyone holding the link may be able to act with the associated identity until the link expires or is revoked.

---

## **Access Control**

The token system enables fine control over access:

* **Public endpoints**: no token required  
* **Protected endpoints**: require valid token  
* **Admin endpoints**: require elevated identity (e.g. Game Master)  
  ---

## **Security Model**

The system ensures:

* signed token verification

* expiration control

* database-stored persistent tokens

* separation between public and protected routes

  ---

## **Current Strengths**

* supports multi-platform identity

* flexible authentication (JWT \+ persistent tokens)

* clean separation between identity and UI

* scalable for future access control systems

  ---

## **Planned Evolution**

The system is designed to support future features:

* Paid access system: determine whether a user can enter a protected feature, what level of access they have, and how long that access remains valid.

* Session-based permissions: allow temporary elevated access and feature unlocking.

* Stronger identity linking logic: improve cross-platform merging and user-level progression.

  ---

## **Why This System Matters**

This system is critical because it:

* connects all user actions to a verified identity

* enables controlled access to features

* supports monetization and scaling

It acts as the backbone of **security**, **personalization**, and **game integrity**.

===== FILE: dmg-doc/technical-implementation/api-endpoint-summary.md =====

# **API Endpoints (Summary)**
## **Purpose**

This section summarizes the implemented backend route groups exposed by the API.

It acts as a clean implementation reference for:

* what route families exist  
* what each route family is used for  
* where the main system actions are exposed

This section complements **System Architecture → API Structure**, which explains the route families conceptually rather than listing the implemented endpoints.

## **Route groups**

### **Admin routes**

#### **Base path**

`/api/v1/admin`

#### **Access level**

Admin-secret protected

#### **Purpose**

Admin routes expose internal monitoring data for the privileged dashboard.

They are used to:

* check system health  
* inspect global economy metrics  
* inspect maintenance status and global clocks

#### **Main endpoints**

* `GET /pulse` → returns system health, global economy totals, and maintenance status for the admin dashboard

---

### **Challenge routes**

#### **Base path**

### `/api/v1/challenges`

#### **Access level**

Mixed:

* GET /:id \= public read-only  
* GET / and GET /delta \= Explorer-token protected \+ entitlement-gated

#### **Purpose**

Challenge routes expose 

* public single-challenge detail pages   
* Authenticated Explorer collection and delta feeds

#### **Main endpoints**

* `GET /` → returns the Explorer challenge collection for an authenticated entitled Explorer session  
* `GET /delta` → returns Explorer challenge updates since a given timestamp  
* `GET /:id` → returns one public challenge by ID

---

### **Clock routes**

#### **Base path**

`/api/v1/clock`

#### **Access level**

Internal scheduled endpoints / cron-protected

#### **Purpose**

Clock routes expose scheduled maintenance entry points.

They are used to:

* trigger daily maintenance securely through a scheduled service  
* apply daily clock-based system rules

#### **Main endpoints**

* `POST /run-daily-maintenance` → runs the daily maintenance process

---

### **Command routes**
#### **Base path**

`/api/v1/command`

#### **Access level**

Authenticated command ingress

#### **Purpose**

Command routes expose the main backend entrypoint for external command execution.

#### **They are used to:**

* receive command payloads from chat-connected systems  
* authenticate and resolve the acting user  
* apply rate limiting before execution  
* forward commands into the centralized dispatcher

#### **Main endpoints**

* `POST /` → main command entrypoint for external command execution

---

### **Game Master routes**

#### **Base path**

/api/v1/gamemaster

#### **Access level**

Privileged Game Master control

#### **Purpose**

Game Master routes expose privileged control endpoints reserved for Game Master actions.

They are used to:

* execute a challenge manually

* force challenge status changes

#### **Main endpoints**

* `POST /challenge/execute` → manually launches a challenge  
* `PUT /challenge/:challengeId/status` → forces a challenge status update

---

### **Reference routes**

#### **Base path**

`/api/v1/references`

#### **Access level**

Public helper endpoint

#### **Purpose**

Reference routes expose metadata helpers for external reference links.

They are used to:

* resolve a readable title for a public reference URL

#### **Main endpoints**

* `GET /title` → resolves the title of a reference URL

---

### **Stream routes**
#### **Base path**

`/api/v1/stream`

#### **Access level**

Mixed: internal webhook \+ public read endpoint

#### **Purpose**

Stream routes expose stream-state webhooks and stream status read endpoints.

They are used to:

* process live / offline webhook events  
* expose global stream state and stream statistics

#### **Main endpoints**

* `POST /live` → processes the stream live event  
* `POST /offline` → processes the stream offline event  
* `GET /stats` → returns current stream state and global stream statistics

---

### **Token routes**
#### **Base path**

`/api/v1/token`

#### **Access level**

Token-based protected access

#### **Purpose**

Token routes expose secure token verification flows for protected frontend pages.

They are used to:

* verify secure challenge submission access  
* verify secure Explorer access  
* return identity and access-related context to the frontend

#### **Main endpoints**

* `POST /verify-challengesubmitform` → verifies a submission token and returns identity plus submission context  
* `POST /verify-explorer` → verifies an Explorer token and processes Explorer access rules

---

### **User routes**

#### **Base path**

`/api/v1/user`

#### **Access level**

Authenticated user actions

#### **Purpose**

User routes expose authenticated player actions.

They are used to:

* submit challenges  
* quote and confirm pushes  
* digout archived challenges  
* disrupt  
* retrieve active challenges  
* remove a challenge  
* process both legacy and web-based submission flows

#### **Player action endpoints**

* `POST /submit` → legacy authenticated challenge submission route  
* `POST /submit/web` → web-form challenge submission route  
* `POST /push/quote` → generates a push quote  
* `POST /push/confirm` → confirms and applies a push  
* `POST /digout` → revives an archived challenge  
* `POST /disrupt` → executes the current placeholder disrupt action  
* `POST /challenge/remove` → removes an active challenge as its author and applies refund distribution logic


===== FILE: dmg-doc/technical-implementation/backend-logic.md =====

# **Backend Logic**
## **Purpose**

The backend logic layer applies the rules of the product.

It is responsible for turning stored data and incoming actions into actual system behavior.

This includes:

* challenge lifecycle enforcement  
* cost calculation  
* stream-state-dependent logic  
* clock progression  
* access validation  
* synchronization with external systems

## **Core principle**

The backend applies the core rules of the product in dedicated service layers rather than inside frontend pages.

This means:

* the main product rules are applied in backend services  
* time-based behavior is handled in dedicated backend logic  
* actions that affect multiple records are coordinated in backend logic  
* route handlers translate known service failures into consistent HTTP responses  
* the system behaves consistently across chat, web pages, and admin flows

---

## **Main logic areas**

### **Challenge logic**
Handled primarily in `challengeService.ts`.

This logic controls:

* challenge submission  
* push quote and push confirmation  
* digout  
* removals  
* disruption placeholder logic  
* execution launch  
* 21-minute session progression and completion checks  
* challenge archival  
* status changes

Why it matters:

* this is where the core challenge mechanics are enforced  
* it connects challenge lifecycle, NUMBERS spending, stream metrics, and event dispatching

### **Autonomous session scheduler**
Session progression is checked by an autonomous scheduler rather than being tracked manually.

This works as follows:

* the scheduler checks execution state at a fixed interval

* it verifies whether the current session has reached the 21-minute threshold

* once the threshold is reached, it increments the session count and stops active execution

* if the final required session is reached, the challenge is marked as completed

* additional sessions require manual re-execution by the Game Master

* actual live execution is tracked by the isExecuting flag, which is separate from the broader lifecycle state In Progress

Why it matters:

* it makes session progression time-based rather than manually tracked  
* it enforces the 21-minute execution unit consistently  
* it keeps execution stopping and completion logic reliable across sessions

### **Clock and maintenance logic**

Handled primarily in `clockService.ts`.

This logic controls:

* daily maintenance  
* user daily tick processing  
* ONE\_OFF contiguity enforcement  
* recurring cadence enforcement  
* archival checks tied to maintenance conditions

Why it matters:

* it applies the product’s time rules centrally  
* it keeps challenge progression, user counters, and maintenance behavior synchronized

### **Stream-state logic**

Handled primarily in `streamService.ts`.

This logic controls:

* live / offline transitions  
* stream session creation and finalization  
* global Stream Day advancement  
* per-challenge Stream Day advancement for active challenges  
* in-memory stream-state recovery after restart

Why it matters:

* stream state affects challenge launch context, live pricing rules, Stream Day advancement, and active-challenge day progression

* this logic ensures Stream Days only advance when real stream activity happens

* it also allows the backend to restore its live-stream state after restart by loading the current active session back into memory from the database

### **Token and identity logic**

Handled primarily in `jwtService.ts` and related token routes.

This logic controls:

* JWT generation  
* token verification  
* perennial token lookup  
* duration validation and normalization  
* identity payload handling

Why it matters:

* it ensures protected actions are tied to verified identity  
* it supports both temporary and persistent access flows

### **Authentication and request identity resolution**
Handled primarily in `authMiddleware.ts` together with `findOrCreateUser()` in `userService.ts`.

This logic controls:

* reading the external platform identity from the incoming command payload  
* resolving the matching internal DMG user from platformName \+ platformId  
* creating a new User / Account pair when the identity does not yet exist  
* attaching the resolved internal DMG user identity and request context before command execution  
* enforcing Game Master\-only access on privileged routes

Why it matters:

* it turns external chat-platform identity into authenticated internal DMG identity before backend logic runs  
* it allows first-time users to enter the system simply by sending a command  
* it keeps command execution tied to a resolved internal user rather than raw external payload alone  
* it makes the chat command layer the practical runtime entrypoint into the product

### **Lumia balance synchronization**
Handled primarily through `lumiaService.ts` together with challenge-related service logic.

This logic controls:

* authoritative NUMBERS deductions and additions  
* synchronization between external platform balances and local database state  
* balance updates after paid actions succeed

Why it matters:

* Lumia acts as the external source of truth for platform balances  
* the backend must keep local records aligned with that external balance state  
* paid actions depend on this synchronization to remain reliable

### **Transaction and payment synchronization logic**

Handled across service functions that combine:

* external balance calls

* database updates

* temporary pre-confirmation records

* deletion of temporary quote records after successful confirmation

This logic controls:

* optimistic local balance pre-checks based on the latest balance stored in the DMG database, before calling the Lumia API

* paid-action execution after balance confirmation

* multi-record database updates after payment success

* cleanup of temporary push quote records

Why it matters:

* optimistic local balance pre-checks reduce unnecessary external balance calls and stop obviously invalid actions early before full transaction execution

* it keeps local state and external balances aligned

* it uses Prisma transactions, so paid actions either complete fully or fail without leaving partial database updates

### **User activity and identity resolution**

Handled primarily in `userService.ts`.

This logic controls:

* user creation and account creation  
* platform-account lookup  
* user activity recording  
* Game Master identity checks  
* user statistics aggregation

Why it matters:

* it connects external platform identity to internal DMG identity  
* it keeps user activity and account linking consistent across the system

### **Event dispatching**
Handled in `eventService.ts`.

This logic publishes challenge-related events so other parts of the system can react to meaningful state changes such as:

* submission  
* execution  
* session completion  
* digout  
* removal  
* GM activation

Why it matters:

* it separates core state changes from downstream reactions  
* it allows notifications, console subscribers, and future integrations to react without being hard-wired into the core service logic  
* it prepares the system for future subscribers without coupling them directly to challengeService or scheduler logic  
* subscribers

### **Rate limiting and infrastructure support**
Handled in `upstashService.ts`.

This logic provides Redis-backed rate limiting for command flows and helps protect the system from excessive repeated requests.

Why it matters:

* it reduces abuse risk  
* it protects command-driven interaction during live usage

### **Command dispatch logic**
Handled primarily in `commandDispatcher.ts`.

This logic controls:

* receiving normalized command payloads from the dedicated command route  
* parsing command arguments  
* routing each command to the correct service function  
* keeping command handling centralized behind one backend entry point

Why it matters:

* it gives the system one consistent command-processing layer  
* it makes authentication and rate limiting easier to apply before command execution  
* it reduces duplication across command sources that use the same backend entry point

### **Reference metadata resolution**

Handled primarily in `referenceMetadata.ts`.

This logic controls:

* validating reference URLs  
* resolving reference titles from supported public sources  
* improving the challenge submission flow by reducing manual entry

Supported sources currently include:

* YouTube  
* Vimeo  
* SoundCloud  
* Spotify  
* Wikipedia  
* generic public pages

Why it matters:

* it improves submission UX without changing the core game logic  
* it makes reference-based challenges easier to create and review  
* it keeps title-fetching behavior centralized in one helper layer

---

## **Important implementation choices**

### **UTC-only time handling**

Time-sensitive logic uses UTC as the reference standard.

This affects:

* daily resets  
* maintenance  
* Real Day progression  
* Stream Day logic  
* quote expiration  
* consistent timestamps across multi-step service operations

Why it matters:

* it prevents timezone drift and daylight-saving ambiguity  
* it gives the system one consistent time standard for all clocks and resets

### **Canonical challenge activity timestamp**

Each challenge keeps one canonical last-activity timestamp.

This timestamp is refreshed whenever a meaningful change happens to the challenge, such as:

* submission  
* push  
* execution  
* completion  
* archival  
* removal  
* other state-changing actions

Why it matters:

* it gives the system one reliable reference point for recency  
* it supports synchronization, ordering, monitoring, and incremental frontend updates

### **Precision timing rules**

Different timing needs use different time precision levels.

This includes:

* standardized UTC timestamps for multi-step service operations  
* millisecond-level timing for short expiration windows such as push quotes

Why it matters:

* it keeps multi-record updates consistent inside one operation  
* it makes short-lived expiration logic reliable where higher precision is required

### **Two-clock logic**
The backend treats Real Days and Stream Days as different clocks.

This means:

* Real Days advance through maintenance  
* Stream Days advance only when a qualifying stream day occurs  
* challenge progression and archival can depend on actual stream activity rather than passive time alone

Why it matters:

* it preserves the product’s distinction between system time and execution effort

### **Just-in-time daily reset behavior**

Some daily user resets are not applied through a full database-wide midnight reset.

Instead, they are checked and refreshed when the user next interacts after the reset boundary.

This currently affects:

* daily submission cost scaling

Why it matters:

* it reduces unnecessary background load  
* it keeps daily reset behavior predictable without forcing full-system rewrites at reset time

### Two-stage push flow
Push execution is split into two stages:

1. quote generation  
2. quote confirmation

This means:

* the cost is calculated first  
* a temporary quote is stored briefly  
* the final push is only committed after confirmation

Why it matters:

* it makes quadratic push cost explicit before payment  
* it supports controlled confirmation and atomic execution

### **BigInt financial handling**
Large financial ledgers use `BigInt`.

This is used for:

* game-wide totals  
* large accumulated NUMBERS metrics  
* community chest and other system-wide financial totals  
* other long-term aggregate financial counters

Because JSON does not serialize BigInt values by default, the backend includes explicit serialization handling before returning these values to the frontend.

Why it matters:

* it prevents overflow risk in large financial ledgers  
* it keeps long-term economy tracking safe as the system grows

### **Central rule configuration**

Core rule values are centralized in `gameConfig.ts`.

This includes:

* base costs  
* timing constants  
* percentage rules  
* token duration limits  
* admin/system identifiers  
* precision helpers used in BigInt calculations

Why it matters:

* it keeps core game rules explicit and editable in one place  
* it reduces hard-coded rule duplication across services  
* it makes balancing and system adjustment easier over time

---

## **Relationship with other technical layers**

This backend logic sits between:

* the database layer  
* the API route layer  
* external integrations such as Lumia  
* frontend interfaces that trigger system actions

It is the rule-enforcement layer of the product.

## **Why this backend logic matters**

This is where DMG becomes an actual system rather than a static website or database.

It ensures that:

* product rules are enforceable  
* actions have consistent consequences  
* time, economy, identity, and execution stay synchronized  
* live interaction can scale without relying on manual control

===== FILE: dmg-doc/technical-implementation/database.md =====

# **Database**
## **Purpose**

The database stores the persistent state of the product.  
 It holds the core records needed to track:

* user identity  
* platform accounts  
* challenges  
* pushes  
* stream sessions  
* maintenance clocks  
* persistent access tokens

It is the durable system layer that allows DMG to preserve history, apply rules consistently, and recover state across sessions.

## **Core design principle**

The database is structured around a few key separations:

* **internal user identity** is separated from **external platform accounts**  
* **challenge state** is separated from **push** **history**  
* **global time** **tracking** is separated from **individual stream sessions**  
* **temporary quote records** are separated from **finalized transactions**

This keeps identity, challenge state, time tracking, and temporary pre-confirmation records clearly separated.

---

## **Main models**

### **User**
Represents the central internal identity of a player in DMG.

It stores:

* the internal user ID  
* game-wide participation counters  
* long-term activity history  
* aggregate NUMBERS metrics  
* progression-related state

Why it exists:

* unify activity across platforms  
* keep global user history in one place  
* support user-level totals, progression, and long-term activity tracking

### **Special system record**
User ID 1 is used as the **global ledger record** (“World User”).

It is used to track:

* game-wide NUMBERS totals  
* Community Chest totals  
* system-wide economy counters tied to spending, refunds, and redistribution

Why it matters:

* it gives the system one central record for global economy tracking  
* it keeps player-level activity separate from system-level financial totals

### **Tracked user metrics**

The `User` model also stores long-term per-user game metrics such as:

* total digouts executed  
* total pushes executed  
* total disrupts executed  
* total challenges submitted  
* total removals executed  
* total NUMBERS spent  
* total value received from removals  
* total value caused by removals  
* total value directed to the Community Chest  
* total value returned to pushers

Why it matters:

* these metrics make user activity, contribution, and economic impact visible over time  
* they support progression, analytics, and future user-facing history features

### **Account**
Represents one platform-specific identity linked to a user.

It stores:

* platform name  
* platform ID  
* mutable username / display name  
* platform-specific NUMBERS balance  
* platform-level activity timestamps

Why it exists:

* separate external identity from internal identity  
* track balances and activity per platform  
* support cross-platform identity linking

### **StreamStat**

Represents the global system clocks and maintenance watermark.

It stores:

* Real Days  
* Stream Days  
* last maintenance timestamp

Why it exists:

* support the two-watermark clock system  
* store the reference point used by daily maintenance  
* keep global time-based mechanics consistent

### **Challenge**

Represents the canonical record of a challenge.

It stores:

* challenge content  
* proposer identity snapshots  
* lifecycle state  
* duration type  
* cadence state  
* execution progress  
* timestamps  
* challenge-level economy metrics

Why it exists:

* act as the central state record for the challenge lifecycle  
* support ranking, execution, archival, and history

### **Push**

Represents finalized promotion history for a challenge.

It stores:

* which user pushed  
* which challenge was pushed  
* cost paid  
* quantity  
* timestamp

Why it exists:

* preserve push history as a permanent record  
* support challenge ranking and user-level push tracking  
* store each finalized push as its own record instead of only keeping a challenge-level total

### **TempQuote**
Represents a temporary push quote before confirmation.

It stores:

* quoted push cost  
* target challenge  
* target user  
* requested quantity  
* creation timestamp  
* lock state

Why it exists:

* support the two-stage push flow  
* separate price calculation from final execution  
* allow short-lived quote validation before committing the action

### **Stream**
Represents one stream session.

It stores:

* session start and end timestamps  
* duration  
* per-session activity totals  
* session-level economy metrics  
* processing state

Why it exists:

* preserve stream session history  
* track per-session activity and economy metrics  
* distinguish an active stream session from a fully finalized one

### **PerennialToken**
Represents a persistent authentication token stored in the database.

It stores:

* token value  
* linked user  
* linked account  
* active / inactive state  
* creation timestamp

Why it exists:

* support persistent access flows beyond short JWT sessions  
* allow manually managed token-based access  
* prepare the system for more flexible entitlement and feature-access models

## **Why this database structure matters**

This structure keeps DMG understandable at the data level.

It allows the system to:

* separate identity, activity, economy, and time clearly  
* preserve history without mixing temporary and permanent state  
* support cross-platform continuity  
* apply system rules on top of clearly separated records for identity, challenges, time, and transactions


===== FILE: dmg-doc/technical-implementation/integrations.md =====

# **Integrations**
## **Purpose**

This section documents the external systems DMG relies on to operate across live platforms, community channels, and web tools.

These integrations are used to:

* connect DMG to live chat environments  
* reuse existing loyalty and balance infrastructure at launch  
* extend participation across live and offline channels

They are not the core product logic themselves, but they make the product usable in real conditions.

---

## **Lumia**
### **Purpose**

Lumia is used as the launch-layer bridge between DMG and supported livestream platforms.

### **What it does**

Lumia currently provides two critical capabilities:

* an existing loyalty-points system used as the initial NUMBERS layer  
* a shared command-listening layer across Lumia-supported livestream platforms

This means Lumia can:

* grant points through watch time  
* apply reward modifiers based on user status such as follower, subscriber tier, VIP, or moderator where the connected platform and Lumia support it  
* listen for supported chat commands  
* send command payloads with user identity data to the main command ingress route

### **Role in the system**

Lumia reduces the amount of custom infrastructure DMG needs at launch.

It allows DMG to:

* start with an already working points system instead of building one from scratch  
* reuse an existing live chat-listening layer across supported platforms  
* connect paid actions to an external balance authority rather than treating the local database as the final balance source

### **Why it matters**

This integration is critical because it makes the product operational much faster.

It allows DMG to launch with:

* watch-time-based NUMBERS earning  
* platform-linked reward modifiers  
* supported chat commands routed to the main command ingress route

It also leaves room for future evolution if DMG later moves more of that logic in-house.

---

## **Discord**

### **Purpose**

Discord is the main offline community hub for DMG.

### **What it does**

At baseline, Discord provides:

* a persistent community space outside live sessions  
* continuity between streams  
* a place where ideas, discussion, and coordination can continue when the stream is offline

Its product value for DMG comes mainly from the planned Discord bot layer.

### **Planned Discord bot layer**
A dedicated Discord bot is planned as the main offline interaction layer.

Its role would be to:

* authenticate users against their livestream-platform identity

* listen for supported offline commands

* send valid command payloads to the main command ingress route

* restrict or disable certain offline commands when the stream is live, so live participation remains concentrated on livestream platforms

### **Role in the system**

Discord gives DMG a persistent hub, while the planned bot would turn that hub into an actual offline gameplay layer.

Together, they would allow DMG to:

* stay socially active between streams

* support structured interaction outside live sessions

* reuse the same command model across live and offline channels

### **Why it matters**

Without the bot, Discord is mainly a community hub; with it, Discord becomes part of the DMG interaction model.

That makes offline participation operational rather than only social.

---

## **Streaming platforms**

### **Purpose**

Streaming platforms are the live participation surfaces where DMG runs in real time.

### **What they do**

Streaming platforms provide:

* live chat environments  
* platform-level user identity  
* the real-time context where commands and participation happen during a stream

Depending on the platform and the Lumia integration, they can also support:

* watch-time-based reward logic  
* subscription-aware reward modifiers  
* live participation tied directly to stream state

### **Role in the system**

Streaming platforms are where DMG becomes a live product.

They provide:

* the real-time participation layer  
* the original source of many commands and user actions  
* the live context that drives stream-state-dependent mechanics such as discounts, execution flow, and activity tracking

### **Why it matters**

These integrations allow DMG to function as a multi-platform livestream product rather than a single-site system.

They are the live surfaces on which the product is actually experienced.

---

## **Integration model**

These integrations work together as one operational stack.

At a high level:

* streaming platforms provide the live participation surfaces  
* Lumia provides the launch-layer loyalty and command bridge across supported livestream platforms  
* Discord provides the main offline hub and the future offline bot layer

This allows DMG to operate:

* during live streams  
* between live streams  
* across multiple participation channels without reducing everything to one interface

## **Why this integration layer matters**

The integration layer connects backend rules to real user environments.

It allows DMG to:

* launch on top of existing live infrastructure  
* preserve continuity across live and offline participation  
* support a cross-platform experience while keeping one central system logic 

===== FILE: dmg-doc/technical-implementation/streaming-production-setup.md =====

# **Streaming / Production Setup**
### **Purpose**

This section defines the production environment supporting the livestream system.

### **It includes:**

* streaming software  
* camera setup  
* visual tools  
* audio setup  
* stream access utilities  
* backup plans

### **Role in the system**

This setup supports the live layer of the product and ensures the interactive system can run reliably in production

### **Current production setup**

The livestream system currently runs on the following production setup:

* **Streaming Software:** OBS Studio and Aitum Multistream.

* **Overlays:** Segmented overlay design with dedicated spaces, initially implemented to compensate for GoPro feed quality constraints in a 1920×1080 stream

* **Rate Control:** ABR (Adaptive Bitrate)

* **Cameras:** 

  * Main camera: GoPro HERO 8 (via GoPro Webcam mode), with plans to upgrade

  * Secondary camera: GoPro HERO 7 (via Elgato Cam Link)

* **Visual Tools:** Social Stream Ninja (chat overlay), Lumia Stream (hands-free lighting effects)

* **Audio:** OBS microphone settings include noise suppression, noise gate, compressor, and EQ adjustments for clarity

* **Transitions:** Stinger transitions in development

* **Live Access:** QR codes for live access to challenge lists, stats, and the donation page

* **Internet connection**: 376.8 Mbps down / 279.6 Mbps up / 17 ms latency

* **Hardware:** MacBook Pro (2019, 16-inch) with external TV used as monitor

### **Repository note**

Large audio assets are managed through Git LFS, so new development environments must initialize Git LFS before working with the full media set.


===== FILE: dmg-doc/technical-implementation/transaction-handling.md =====

# **Transaction Handling**
## **Purpose**

This section explains how DMG handles multi-step operations that affect both local database state and external balance state.

It focuses on:

* Prisma transactions  
* external balance synchronization  
* rollback behavior  
* failure handling

## **Why this matters**

Many important DMG actions do not update only one record.

They can affect:

* user metrics  
* account balances  
* challenge state  
* stream metrics  
* temporary quote records  
* global economy totals

Because of this, transaction handling is critical to system reliability.

## **Prisma transactions**

DMG uses Prisma transactions for actions that update multiple database records as part of one operation.

This is used for flows such as:

* challenge submission  
* push confirmation  
* digout  
* removals  
* disruption placeholder spending  
* execution state changes  
* automatic session tick updates

### **Purpose in the system**

Prisma transactions ensure that related database updates succeed together or fail together.

This prevents partial local writes such as:

* a challenge submission completing without the related user, account, stream, and global-ledger updates  
* a push confirmation updating challenge totals without updating the matching user, account, stream, and quote records  
* a digout or removal updating challenge state without the matching economy and activity records

## **External balance synchronization**

Some paid actions also depend on Lumia, which acts as the external balance authority.

This means the system often combines:

* a local optimistic balance check  
* an external Lumia deduction or addition  
* local database updates after the external call succeeds

### **Purpose in the system**

This keeps DMG’s local records aligned with the external balance source rather than treating the local database as the final authority for platform balances.

## **Rollback behavior**

When a database transaction fails, the local database changes inside that transaction are not committed.

This means the system avoids partial local outcomes such as:

* challenge state updated without the matching user update  
* stream metrics updated without the matching account update  
* quote confirmation applied without the full set of related writes

### **Important distinction**

Rollback protection applies to local database operations.

External calls are outside the database transaction itself.

Because of this, the system is designed to call external balance operations at controlled points in the flow before final local commit logic is completed.

## **Failure handling**
The backend handles failures explicitly at both the service layer and the route layer.

This includes:

* checking required inputs and action conditions before costly or multi-step operations run  
* rejecting clearly invalid actions before external calls or multi-record updates begin  
* mapping known service errors to clear HTTP responses  
* cleaning up temporary records when needed  
* preventing partially completed local state changes

### **Examples**

* an expired push quote is rejected and removed  
* an insufficient local balance check stops the action before the external call  
* an external Lumia failure stops the paid action before local completion  
* a failed database transaction prevents partial local writes

## **Relationship with Backend Logic**

This section complements Technical Implementation → Backend Logic.

### **Backend Logic explains:**

* what rules the system applies

### **Transaction Handling explains:**

* how the system keeps multi-step operations coherent when those rules are executed

===== BACKEND REPO SNAPSHOT =====

BACKEND SNAPSHOT
===== FILE: /Users/mac/dmg-api/.github/workflows/backup.yml =====

name: Daily Supabase Database Backup

on:
  workflow_dispatch:
  schedule:
    - cron: '0 21 * * *'

jobs:
  backup:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      contents: write

    steps:
      - name: ⬇️ Checkout repository
        uses: actions/checkout@v4
        with:
          fetch-depth: 0 

      - name: ⚙️ Setup Supabase CLI
        uses: supabase/setup-cli@v1
        with:
          version: latest

      # --- NEW STEP: Ensure the directory exists ---
      - name: 📂 Create Backup Directory
        run: mkdir -p supabase/backups

      # --- 1. Backup Roles ---
      - name: 💾 Backup Roles
        run: supabase db dump --db-url "${{ secrets.SUPABASE_DB_URL }}" -f supabase/backups/roles.sql --role-only
        
      # --- 2. Backup Schema ---
      - name: 💾 Backup Schema
        run: supabase db dump --db-url "${{ secrets.SUPABASE_DB_URL }}" -f supabase/backups/schema.sql
        
      # --- 3. Backup Data ---
      - name: 💾 Backup Data
        run: supabase db dump --db-url "${{ secrets.SUPABASE_DB_URL }}" -f supabase/backups/data.sql --data-only --use-copy

      - name: 📅 Commit Backup Files
        uses: stefanzweifel/git-auto-commit-action@v5
        with:
          commit_message: "chore(backup): Daily Supabase DB Backup"
          file_pattern: supabase/backups/*.sql

===== FILE: /Users/mac/dmg-api/prisma/seed.ts =====

// prisma/seed.ts

/**
 * Master Seed Orchestrator
 * This script coordinates the execution of specialized seed scripts.
 * * Order of operations:
 * 1. seedUsers: Performs a destructive TRUNCATE and creates 21 Users / 42 Accounts.
 * 2. seedChallenges: Submits Challenges that form the basis of the Explorer content.
 * 3. seedPushes: Populates the 'pushes' table and synchronizes aggregate counters on Challenges and Users to reflect activity in the Explorer UI.
 * 
 * Each seed script is designed to be idempotent and can be run independently for testing purposes, but this master script ensures the correct order and handles any dependencies between them.
*/

import { PrismaClient } from '@prisma/client';

const prisma = new PrismaClient();

async function runMasterSeed() {
  console.log('-------------------------------------------------------');
  console.log('🌐 PERENNIAL MASTER SEED: Starting Orchestration...');
  console.log('-------------------------------------------------------');

  try {
    // Step 1: Seed Users and Identities
    // This script contains the TRUNCATE logic, so it MUST run first.
    console.log('\n[PHASE 1] Resetting Database & Seeding Users...');
    const { main: seedUsers } = await import('./seedUsers');
    await seedUsers();
    console.log('✅ Phase 1 Complete.');

    // Step 2: Seed Challenges
    // This script relies on the Users/Tokens created in Phase 1.
    console.log('\n[PHASE 2] Seeding 63 Demo Challenges...');
    const { main: seedChallenges } = await import('./seedChallenges');
    await seedChallenges();
    console.log('✅ Phase 2 Complete.');

    // Step 3: Seed Pushes
    // This script populates the push history for the explorer/activity feed.
    console.log('\n[PHASE 3] Seeding Push Notification History...');
    const { main: seedPushes } = await import('./seedPushes');
    await seedPushes();
    console.log('✅ Phase 3 Complete.');

  } catch (error) {
    console.error('\n❌ CRITICAL: Master Seed process failed.');
    console.error(error);
    process.exit(1);
  } finally {
    // Ensure the master client is disconnected
    await prisma.$disconnect();
    console.log('\n-------------------------------------------------------');
    console.log('✨ MASTER SEED COMPLETE');
    console.log('-------------------------------------------------------');
  }
}

// Execute the master seed
runMasterSeed().catch((err) => {
  console.error(err);
  process.exit(1);
});
===== FILE: /Users/mac/dmg-api/prisma/seedChallenges.ts =====

/**
 * Challenge Seeding Script for Perennial Demo Database
 * This script populates the 'challenges' table with 63 challenges (42 Active + 21 Diversified), 
 * simulating user submissions through the service layer to ensure all business logic 
 * and validations (including financial accounting) are applied.
 */

import { PrismaClient, PlatformName, DurationType, CadenceUnit, ChallengeStatus } from '@prisma/client';
import * as challengeService from '../src/services/challengeService'; 
import logger from '../src/logger';

const prisma = new PrismaClient();







function buildSeedCadenceText(
  durationType: DurationType,
  totalSessions: number,
  cadenceUnit: CadenceUnit | null,
  options?: {
    pace?: number;
    timeframeCount?: number;
    customDays?: number;
  }
): string {
  if (durationType === DurationType.ONE_OFF) {
    return `ONE_OFF: ${totalSessions} session(s).`;
  }

  const pace = options?.pace ?? 1;
  const timeframeCount = options?.timeframeCount ?? totalSessions;
  const customDays = options?.customDays ?? 2;
  const paceText = pace === 1 ? 'session' : 'sessions';

  if (cadenceUnit === CadenceUnit.DAILY) {
    return `${pace} ${paceText} per day for ${timeframeCount} days`;
  }

  if (cadenceUnit === CadenceUnit.WEEKLY) {
    return `${pace} ${paceText} per week for ${timeframeCount} weeks`;
  }

  if (cadenceUnit === CadenceUnit.MONTHLY) {
    return `${pace} ${paceText} per month for ${timeframeCount} months`;
  }

  if (cadenceUnit === CadenceUnit.CUSTOM_DAYS) {
    return `${pace} ${paceText} every ${customDays} days then repeat this ${timeframeCount} times`;
  }

  return `ONE_OFF: ${totalSessions} session(s).`;
}







const challengeSeeds = [
  { 
    text: { 
      goal: "Master the Moeller 'whip' technique for effortless power.",

function randomDateBetween(start: Date, end: Date): Date {
  const startMs = start.getTime();
  const endMs = end.getTime();
  return new Date(startMs + Math.random() * (endMs - startMs));
}

function getSeedLifecycleTimestamps(
  status: ChallengeStatus
): {
  submittedAt: Date;
  lastActivityAt: Date;
  completedAt: Date | null;
  cadencePeriodStart: Date | null;
} {
  const now = new Date();

  const submittedAt = randomDateBetween(
    new Date(now.getTime() - 35 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
    new Date(now.getTime() - 2 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
  );

  let lastActivityAt = submittedAt;
  let completedAt: Date | null = null;
  let cadencePeriodStart: Date | null = null;

  switch (status) {
    case ChallengeStatus.ACTIVE:
      lastActivityAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 48 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        now
      );
      break;

    case ChallengeStatus.IN_PROGRESS:
      cadencePeriodStart = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 7 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        new Date(now.getTime() - 12 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
      );
      lastActivityAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        now
      );
      break;

    case ChallengeStatus.FAILED:
      cadencePeriodStart = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 14 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        new Date(now.getTime() - 3 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
      );
      completedAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 5 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        new Date(now.getTime() - 12 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
      );
      lastActivityAt = completedAt;
      break;

    case ChallengeStatus.COMPLETED:
      completedAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 7 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        new Date(now.getTime() - 12 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
      );
      lastActivityAt = completedAt;
      break;

    case ChallengeStatus.ARCHIVED:
      lastActivityAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 21 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        new Date(now.getTime() - 7 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
      );
      break;

    case ChallengeStatus.AUCTIONED:
      lastActivityAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 6 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        new Date(now.getTime() - 1 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
      );
      break;

    case ChallengeStatus.REMOVED:
      lastActivityAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 10 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        new Date(now.getTime() - 2 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000)
      );
      break;

    case ChallengeStatus.UNDER_REVIEW:
      lastActivityAt = randomDateBetween(
        new Date(now.getTime() - 3 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000),
        now
      );
      break;

    default:
      lastActivityAt = submittedAt;
  }

  return {
    submittedAt,
    lastActivityAt,
    completedAt,
    cadencePeriodStart
  };
}






function getSeedStreamDaysSinceActivation(status: ChallengeStatus): number {
  switch (status) {
    case ChallengeStatus.ACTIVE:
      return Math.floor(Math.random() * 14); // 0-13

    case ChallengeStatus.IN_PROGRESS:
      return Math.floor(Math.random() * 14) + 1; // 1-14

    case ChallengeStatus.COMPLETED:
      return Math.floor(Math.random() * 18) + 2; // 2-19

    case ChallengeStatus.FAILED:
      return Math.floor(Math.random() * 18) + 2; // 2-19

    case ChallengeStatus.ARCHIVED:
      return 21;

    case ChallengeStatus.AUCTIONED:
      return Math.floor(Math.random() * 12) + 1; // 1-12

    case ChallengeStatus.REMOVED:
      return Math.floor(Math.random() * 10) + 1; // 1-10

    case ChallengeStatus.UNDER_REVIEW:
      return 0;

    default:
      return 0;
  }
}







export async function main() {
  logger.info('🌱 SEED: Starting FULL Challenge Seeding (63 Challenges)...');

  // 1. Fetch available users restricted to IDs 2 to 20
  const users = await prisma.user.findMany({
    where: { id: { gte: 2, lte: 20 } },
    include: { perennialTokens: true }
  });

  if (users.length === 0) {
    logger.error('❌ No bots (ID 2-20) found. Please run user seed first.');
    return;
  }

  // Combine original 42 seeds with 21 diversified seeds
  const diversifiedSeeds = Array.from({ length: 21 }).map((_, i) => ({
    ...challengeSeeds[i % challengeSeeds.length],
    text: { 
      ...challengeSeeds[i % challengeSeeds.length].text, 
      goal: `[DIVERSIFIED] ${challengeSeeds[i % challengeSeeds.length].text.goal}` 
    }
  }));

  const allSeeds = [...challengeSeeds, ...diversifiedSeeds];
  let seedIndex = 0;

  for (const user of users) {
    const token = user.perennialTokens[0];
    if (!token) continue;

    const submissionsPerUser = Math.ceil(allSeeds.length / users.length);

    for (let i = 0; i < submissionsPerUser; i++) {
      if (seedIndex >= allSeeds.length) break;

      const seed = allSeeds[seedIndex];
      const isOriginal42 = seedIndex < 42;
      
      try {
        const seedCadenceText =
          seed.cadenceText ||
          buildSeedCadenceText(
            seed.durationType,
            seed.totalSessions,
            seed.cadenceUnit || null
          );

        const result = await challengeService.processChallengeSubmission(
          user.id,
          token.platformId,
          token.platformName as PlatformName,
          seed.text,
          seed.totalSessions,
          seed.durationType,
          seedCadenceText || undefined,
          seed.cadenceUnit || undefined
        );

        const cId = result.newChallenge.challengeId;

        const proposerAccount = await prisma.account.findUnique({
          where: {
            platformId_platformName: {
              platformId: token.platformId,
              platformName: token.platformName as PlatformName
            }
          },
          select: {
            username: true,
            platformName: true
          }
        });

        let finalStatus: ChallengeStatus = ChallengeStatus.ACTIVE;
        let failureReason: string | null = null;

        if (!isOriginal42) {
          const roll = Math.random();

          if (roll > 0.78) {
            finalStatus = ChallengeStatus.COMPLETED;
          } else if (roll > 0.62) {
            finalStatus = ChallengeStatus.FAILED;

            const failureReasons = [
              'Insufficient execution consistency across sessions.',
              'Challenge pacing was not sustained over time.',
              'Constraints were repeatedly broken during execution.',
              'Technical validation failed during review.',
              'Challenge was abandoned before completion.'
            ];

            failureReason =
              failureReasons[Math.floor(Math.random() * failureReasons.length)];
          } else if (roll > 0.46) {
            finalStatus = ChallengeStatus.IN_PROGRESS;
          } else if (roll > 0.30) {
            finalStatus = ChallengeStatus.ARCHIVED;
          } else if (roll > 0.20) {
            finalStatus = ChallengeStatus.AUCTIONED;
          } else if (roll > 0.10) {
            finalStatus = ChallengeStatus.REMOVED;
          } else {
            finalStatus = ChallengeStatus.UNDER_REVIEW;
          }
        }

        const {
          submittedAt,
          lastActivityAt,
          completedAt,
          cadencePeriodStart
        } = getSeedLifecycleTimestamps(finalStatus);

        const streamDaysSinceActivation =
          getSeedStreamDaysSinceActivation(finalStatus);

        await prisma.challenge.update({
          where: { challengeId: cId },
          data: {
            status: finalStatus,
            streamDaysSinceActivation,
            timestampSubmitted: submittedAt,
            timestampLastActivityAt: lastActivityAt,
            timestampCompleted: completedAt,
            cadencePeriodStart,
            failureReason,
            proposerUsernameSnapshot: proposerAccount?.username ?? null,
            proposerPlatformNameSnapshot: proposerAccount?.platformName ?? null
          }
        });

        seedIndex++;
      } catch (error) {
        logger.error(`❌ Submission failed for user ${user.id}:`, error);
      }
    }
  }

  const finalCount = await prisma.challenge.count();
  logger.info(`✅ SEED COMPLETE: ${finalCount} Challenges Created.`);
}
===== FILE: /Users/mac/dmg-api/prisma/seedPushes.ts =====

// prisma/seedPushes.ts
/**
 * Push Seeding Script
 * This script seeds push activity across the challenge pool using a weighted distribution of user types
 * (whales, regulars, lurkers) and challenge groups (trending, niche, and selected diversified entries).
 * It also synchronizes aggregate counters on both Challenge and User records so the Explorer reflects the seeded activity accurately.
 */

import { PrismaClient } from '@prisma/client';
import logger from '../src/logger';


const prisma = new PrismaClient();

const getSeedPushQuantity = (): number => {
  const roll = Math.random();

  if (roll > 0.92) return Math.floor(Math.random() * 8) + 5; // 5-12
  if (roll > 0.72) return Math.floor(Math.random() * 3) + 2; // 2-4
  return 1;
};

const calculateSeedPushCost = (
  pushBaseCost: number,
  currentUserPushCount: number,
  quantity: number
): number => {
  let totalCost = BigInt(0);
  const baseCost = BigInt(pushBaseCost);

  for (let i = 1; i <= quantity; i++) {
    const incrementalCount = BigInt(currentUserPushCount + i);
    totalCost += baseCost * (incrementalCount * incrementalCount);
  }

  return Number(totalCost);
};

export async function main() {
  logger.info('🚀 SEED: Starting PUSH (Activity) Seeding...');

  // 1. Fetch Users and Challenges
  const users = await prisma.user.findMany({
    where: { id: { gte: 2, lte: 20 } },
    include: { accounts: true }
  });

  const challenges = await prisma.challenge.findMany({
    orderBy: { challengeId: 'asc' }
  });

  const userChallengePushCounts: Record<string, number> = {};

  if (users.length === 0 || challenges.length === 0) {
    logger.error('❌ Missing dependencies. Run User and Challenge seeds first.');
    return;
  }

  // 2. Distribution Logic
  const whales = users.slice(0, 3);
  const regulars = users.slice(3, 8);
  const lurkers = users.slice(8);

  const activeChallenges = challenges.filter(c => c.status === 'ACTIVE');
  const executionTierChallenges = challenges.filter(c =>
    c.status === 'IN_PROGRESS' ||
    c.status === 'COMPLETED' ||
    c.status === 'FAILED'
  );
  const archivedChallenges = challenges.filter(c => c.status === 'ARCHIVED');
  const auctionedChallenges = challenges.filter(c => c.status === 'AUCTIONED');
  const removedChallenges = challenges.filter(c => c.status === 'REMOVED');
  const underReviewChallenges = challenges.filter(c => c.status === 'UNDER_REVIEW');

  const diversifiedChallenges = challenges.filter(c => {
    const goal =
      typeof c.challengeText === 'object' && c.challengeText && 'goal' in c.challengeText
        ? String((c.challengeText as any).goal || '')
        : '';
    return goal.startsWith('[DIVERSIFIED]');
  });

  const trendingChallenges = [
    ...activeChallenges.slice(0, 4),
    ...executionTierChallenges.slice(0, 6)
  ];

  const nicheChallenges = [
    ...activeChallenges.slice(4, 12),
    ...archivedChallenges.slice(0, 5),
    ...auctionedChallenges.slice(0, 3),
    ...removedChallenges.slice(0, 3),
    ...underReviewChallenges.slice(0, 2),
    ...diversifiedChallenges.slice(0, 8)
  ];

  const pushesToCreate = 150;
  let createdCount = 0;

  // Track aggregates in memory to sync at the end
  const challengeStats: Record<number, { cost: number; pushes: number; uniqueUsers: Set<number> }> = {};
  const userStats: Record<number, { spent: number; pushes: number }> = {};
  let totalPushSpendingGenerated = 0;

  for (let i = 0; i < pushesToCreate; i++) {
    const roll = Math.random();
    let sender = roll > 0.4 ? whales[Math.floor(Math.random() * whales.length)] :
                 roll > 0.1 ? regulars[Math.floor(Math.random() * regulars.length)] :
                 lurkers[Math.floor(Math.random() * lurkers.length)];

    const challengeRoll = Math.random();
    let targetPool = nicheChallenges;

    if (challengeRoll > 0.55) {
      targetPool = trendingChallenges;
    } else if (challengeRoll > 0.25) {
      targetPool = nicheChallenges;
    } else if (challengeRoll > 0.12 && underReviewChallenges.length) {
      targetPool = underReviewChallenges;
    } else if (challengeRoll > 0.06 && removedChallenges.length) {
      targetPool = removedChallenges;
    } else if (auctionedChallenges.length) {
      targetPool = auctionedChallenges;
    }

    const targetChallenge = targetPool[Math.floor(Math.random() * targetPool.length)];

    const quantity = getSeedPushQuantity();
    const trackerKey = `${sender.id}-${targetChallenge.challengeId}`;
    const currentUserPushCount = userChallengePushCounts[trackerKey] ?? 0;
    const cost = calculateSeedPushCost(
      targetChallenge.pushBaseCost,
      currentUserPushCount,
      quantity
    );
    const timestamp = new Date(Date.now() - Math.random() * 30 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);

    try {
      await prisma.push.create({
        data: {
          cost,
          quantity,
          userId: sender.id,
          challengeId: targetChallenge.challengeId,
          timestamp
        }
      });

      userChallengePushCounts[trackerKey] = currentUserPushCount + quantity;

      // Update memory trackers for the Sync Phase
      const cId = targetChallenge.challengeId;
      if (!challengeStats[cId]) challengeStats[cId] = { cost: 0, pushes: 0, uniqueUsers: new Set() };
      challengeStats[cId].cost += cost;
      challengeStats[cId].pushes += quantity;
      challengeStats[cId].uniqueUsers.add(sender.id);

      if (!userStats[sender.id]) userStats[sender.id] = { spent: 0, pushes: 0 };
      userStats[sender.id].spent += cost;
      userStats[sender.id].pushes += quantity;
      
      totalPushSpendingGenerated += cost;

      createdCount++;
    } catch (e) {
      logger.error('❌ Failed to create push:', e);
    }
  }

  // 3. SYNC PHASE: Update Challenge & User Aggregates
  logger.info('🔄 SYNC: Updating Challenge and User counters...');

  for (const [cId, stats] of Object.entries(challengeStats)) {
    await prisma.challenge.update({
      where: { challengeId: Number(cId) },
      data: {
        totalPush: { increment: stats.pushes },
        totalNumbersSpent: { increment: BigInt(stats.cost) },
        uniquePusher: { increment: stats.uniqueUsers.size }
      }
    });
  }

  for (const [uId, stats] of Object.entries(userStats)) {
    await prisma.user.update({
      where: { id: Number(uId) },
      data: {
        totalNumbersSpent: { increment: BigInt(stats.spent) },
        totalPushesExecuted: { increment: stats.pushes }
      }
    });
  }

  // 4. Update Global Ledger (User ID 1)
  // This accounts for all the Push spending generated in this seed.
  // Note: Challenge submission costs were already handled by the challengeService during Phase 2.
  logger.info(`🌐 GLOBAL LEDGER: Incrementing community spending by ${totalPushSpendingGenerated} (Push Activity Only)...`);
  await prisma.user.update({
    where: { id: 1 },
    data: {
      totalNumbersSpentGameWide: { increment: BigInt(totalPushSpendingGenerated) }
    }
  });

  logger.info(`✅ SEED COMPLETE: Generated ${createdCount} pushes and synced all counters.`);
}

// export default main;

// prisma/seedUsers.ts
/**
 * Database Seed Script for development and testing purposes. 
 * This script performs a destructive reset of the database, wiping all existing data and resetting ID counters to ensure a clean slate. 
 * It then creates a predefined set of 21 users and 42 accounts with specific relationships to facilitate testing of various scenarios in the application.
 */

import { PrismaClient, PlatformName } from '@prisma/client';

const prisma = new PrismaClient();

export async function main() {
  console.log('🚀 DESTRUCTIVE RESET: 21 Users / 42 Accounts ID Reset...');
  
  // These match your schema @@map attributes exactly
  const tables = [
    'temp_quotes', 
    'perennial_tokens', 
    'pushes',
    'challenges', 
    'accounts', 
    'users'
  ];

  for (const table of tables) {
    try {
      await prisma.$executeRawUnsafe(`TRUNCATE TABLE "${table}" RESTART IDENTITY CASCADE;`);
    } catch (e) {
      console.error(`❌ Failed to truncate ${table}.`);
    }
  }

  const now = new Date();
  const allPlatforms = [PlatformName.TWITCH, PlatformName.KICK, PlatformName.YOUTUBE];

  // 1. System: Community Chest (ID 1)
  await prisma.user.create({
    data: { 
      id: 1, 
      dailyChallengeResetAt: now,
      totalDigoutsExecuted: 0 
    }
  });

  // 2. Master Identity: User 21 (Linked Triple)
  await prisma.user.create({
    data: {
      id: 21,
      dailyChallengeResetAt: now,
      accounts: {
        create: [
          { platformId: '686071308', platformName: PlatformName.TWITCH, username: '21xhr', currentBalance: 21000000 },
          { platformId: '53255028', platformName: PlatformName.KICK, username: '21xhr', currentBalance: 21000000 },
          { platformId: 'dTQg5JKFl-YiPzg0UQdqng', platformName: PlatformName.YOUTUBE, username: '21xhr', currentBalance: 21000000 },
        ]
      }
    }
  });

  await prisma.perennialToken.create({
    data: { 
      token: 'master_demo_token', 
      userId: 21, 
      platformId: '686071308', 
      platformName: PlatformName.TWITCH 
    }
  });

  // 3. Bots: Users 2 through 20 (Targeting 42 total accounts)
  let remainingAccountSlots = 39;

  for (let i = 2; i <= 20; i++) {
    const isLastBot = i === 20;
    let accountCount = isLastBot 
      ? remainingAccountSlots 
      : Math.min(Math.floor(Math.random() * 3) + 1, remainingAccountSlots - (20 - i));
    
    if (accountCount < 1) accountCount = 1; 
    remainingAccountSlots -= accountCount;

    const shuffledPlatforms = [...allPlatforms].sort(() => Math.random() - 0.5);
    const selectedPlatforms = shuffledPlatforms.slice(0, accountCount);

    const userData = await prisma.user.create({
      data: {
        id: i,
        dailyChallengeResetAt: now,
        accounts: {
          create: selectedPlatforms.map((plat) => {
            // APPLYING SOLO PREFIX LOGIC
            const isSolo = accountCount === 1;
            const prefix = isSolo ? 'solo_' : 'linked_';
            
            return {
              platformId: `${prefix}${plat.toLowerCase()}_${i}`,
              platformName: plat,
              username: `${getStrategyName(accountCount)}_${plat}_${i}`,
              currentBalance: 21000000,
            };
          })
        }
      },
      include: { accounts: true }
    });

    await prisma.perennialToken.create({
      data: { 
        token: `test_token_${i}`, 
        userId: i, 
        platformId: userData.accounts[0].platformId, 
        platformName: userData.accounts[0].platformName 
      }
    });
  }

  const userCount = await prisma.user.count();
  const accCount = await prisma.account.count();
  console.log(`✅ SUCCESS: Created ${userCount} Users and ${accCount} Accounts.`);
  console.log(`🤖 Solo accounts now have "solo_" prefix in platformId.`);
}

function getStrategyName(count: number): string {
  if (count === 1) return 'Solo';
  if (count === 2) return 'Duo';
  return 'Triple';
}

// config/sourcesConfig.ts
/**
 * TRUSTED_SOURCES defines the whitelist for the Automated Profiling system.
 * Links from these domains are automatically approved and may trigger metadata fetching.
 */
export const TRUSTED_SOURCES = {
  VIDEO: [
    'youtube.com',
    'youtu.be',
    'vimeo.com'
  ],
  AUDIO: [
    'spotify.com',
    'music.youtube.com',
    'soundcloud.com',
    'bandcamp.com',
    'deezer.com',
    'tidal.com',
    'qobuz.com',
    'suno.com',
    'udio.com'
  ],
  WIKI: [
    'wikipedia.org',
    'britannica.com'
  ],
  DOCUMENT: [
    'drive.google.com',
    'dropbox.com'
  ]
};

/**
 * Checks if a given URL belongs to the trusted whitelist for its type.
 */
export const isTrustedUrl = (type: string, url: string): boolean => {
  if (!url) return true; // Empty URLs (like in OTHER) are technically trusted
  const typeKey = type.toUpperCase() as keyof typeof TRUSTED_SOURCES;
  const whitelist = TRUSTED_SOURCES[typeKey];
  if (!whitelist) return false;
  
  try {
    const domain = new URL(url).hostname.replace('www.', '');
    return whitelist.some(trusted => domain.includes(trusted));
  } catch {
    return false;
  }
};

// src/eventSubscribers/consoleLogger.ts
// This demonstrates how to create modules that react to the events.

import { ChallengeEvents, subscribeToChallengeEvent } from '../services/eventService';
import { Challenge } from '@prisma/client';

// Define the logic that runs when a SESSION_TICKED event fires
const handleSessionTicked = (challenge: Challenge) => {

// Enables graceful error handling for async routes, 
// preventing the application from crashing on unhandled async exceptions.
import 'express-async-errors';

// ----------------------------------------------------------------------
// GLOBAL BIGINT SERIALIZATION
// ----------------------------------------------------------------------
// Fixes the "Do not know how to serialize a BigInt" error thrown by Express/JSON.stringify
// when data from Prisma/database is sent to the client.
(BigInt.prototype as any).toJSON = function() {
    // Converts BigInts to Strings for safe transport via JSON.
    return this.toString(); 
};

import cors from 'cors';

import prisma from './prisma'; 
import adminRoutes from './routes/adminRoutes';
import challengesRoutes from './routes/challengesRoutes';
import clockRoutes from './routes/clockRoutes';
import commandRoutes from './routes/commandRoutes';

// --- Server Setup ---
const app = express();
// Ensure PORT is always a number by casting the entire expression.
const PORT = Number(process.env.PORT || 3000);

// --- Middleware ---
// Define the allowed origins for CORS (Used for production reference)
const PROD_ORIGIN = "https://dmg-webapp.vercel.app";
// Note: DEV_ORIGINS is only used for logging/debugging context now, the main rule is below.
const DEV_ORIGINS = [
    "http://localhost:3001",
    "http://localhost:5500",
    "http://127.0.0.1:5500",
    "http://192.168.1.37:*"
];

// CORS Configuration (Must come before app.use(express.json()))
const corsOptions = {
    origin: (origin: string | undefined, callback: (err: Error | null, allow?: boolean) => void) => {
        const isProduction = process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production';
        
        // 1. Always allow requests with no origin (like ThunderClient or mobile apps)
        if (!origin) return callback(null, true);

        if (isProduction) {
            // 2. WHITELIST: Add your local IP here so Vercel accepts your local tests
            const allowedOrigins = [
                PROD_ORIGIN, 
                "http://localhost:5500", 
                "http://127.0.0.1:5500",
                "http://192.168.1.37:5500" // Your current local IP
            ];

            if (allowedOrigins.includes(origin)) {
                callback(null, true);
            } else {
                // If someone else tries to host your explorer on their site, Vercel blocks them.
                callback(new Error('CORS Blocked: Origin not in Whitelist'), false);
            }
        } else {
            // 3. In local dev mode, just allow everything for ease of use
            callback(null, true);
        }
    },
    methods: 'GET,HEAD,PUT,PATCH,POST,DELETE',
    allowedHeaders: ['Content-Type', 'X-Admin-Secret', 'Authorization'], 
    credentials: true,
    optionsSuccessStatus: 204
};
app.use(cors(corsOptions)); // Apply CORS Middleware
app.use(express.json());

// --- Application Routers (API Endpoints) ---
app.use('/api/v1/admin', adminRoutes);
app.use('/api/v1/challenges', challengesRoutes)
app.use('/api/v1/clock', clockRoutes);
app.use('/api/v1/command', commandRoutes);
app.use('/api/v1/gamemaster', gamemasterRoutes);
app.use('/api/v1/references', referenceRoutes);
app.use('/api/v1/stream', streamRoutes);
app.use('/api/v1/token', tokenRoutes);
app.use('/api/v1/user', userRoutes); 

// --- Basic Health Check Route ---
app.get('/', async (req: Request, res: Response) => {
  try {
    await prisma.$connect();
    res.status(200).json({
      message: "Drummer Manager API is running successfully!",
      status: "OK",
      dbStatus: "Connected to Supabase", 
      timestamp: new Date().toISOString()
    });
  } catch (error) {
    res.status(500).json({
      message: "Drummer Manager API is running, but database connection failed.",
      status: "ERROR",
      dbStatus: "Failed to connect",
      timestamp: new Date().toISOString()
    });
  }
});


// --- Start the server Function ---
/**
 * Executes state initialization and starts the HTTP listener.
 */
async function startServer() {
  
  try {
    // 🚨 State Initialization: Must run and await before the server starts & listens for requests.
    await initializeStreamState(); 
    startChallengeScheduler();
    initializeConsoleSubscribers();
    initializeNotificationService();
    
  } catch (error) {
    console.error("CRITICAL ERROR: Failed during application state initialization (initializeStreamState). Server cannot start.", error);
    process.exit(1);
  }

  // --- Start the server ---
  const HOST = '0.0.0.0'; // To bind to all interfaces

  // --- Start the server ---
  app.listen(PORT, HOST, () => {
    console.log(`\n🚀 Drummer Manager API is live and network accessible at http://${HOST}:${PORT}`);
    console.log(`Mode: ${process.env.NODE_ENV || 'development'}`);
  });
}


// Call the async function to begin the startup sequence.
startServer();
